RATING: 6.5
This game indeed meets the expectations of a fun pirate game. It may be difficult to win as a pirate, but I don't think that takes away from the sheer enjoyment (and surely a house-rule could fix this). There's a simple routine to playing, a rhythm that might become dry after several games - and simply sailing about buying and selling is early on an obvious strategy. But this game demands more than selling bananas and tobacco. For me, you need to raid merchant ships and escape thuggish frigates from nations with a bounty on your head. This is my favorite pirate/ship game so far.

RATING: 3
Oh my god. How much downtime can there be in a game… Everybody played quick and still it felt like all you did was wait and wait and wait. Then you decided to go to the toilet and chase the badger out of its hole. And when you get back it is still not your turn.

Merchants and Marauders could have been a fun pick up and deliver game but it would have required the game being stripped all unnecessary fluff like the rumors, glory cards, zillions of ship attributes, and most importantly the over complicated and long battle would have needed simplifying. Now a single battle could take 15 minutes and all the while players not involved in the battle have nothing to do.

Mechanically there is nothing broken and there are no fatal design errors. The whole game just feels like all the mechanics were taken from a board game published 40 years ago. There is nothing innovative or elegant. Everything is slow and clunky. 

The only good thing I have to say about Merchants and Marauders is that it looks good and I really like the theme. Completing missions, trading goods and sinking ships is also fun, but it would need to happen at a pace 100x faster.

RATING: 5.5
I had been looking forward to giving M&M a try for quite some time and recently got the chance to play a game with a friend's copy.  I went in expecting a 3-hour marathon of high seas intrigue and ship-to-ship combat.  Instead, the game finished in under 2 hours and the winner had reached 11 Glory, with the other 3 competitors at 2, 2, and 1 Glory each.  Needless to say, this was a less than satisfying game.

While I was one of the also-rans in this particular game, I am not so competitive that losing a game will sour my impressions of it.  Instead, what bothered me was that the game was no contest.  The winner had everything go his way.  Granted, he made good choices and took advantage of his luck, but he so outpaced everyone else that it killed any sense of tension in the game.  Perhaps the other players could have set out to try to sink him, but he was the first to gain a big ship and completely outclassed everyone else.  I expected M&M to have a high degree of luck involved, but it was still disappointing to have all the luck go in one player's favor.  I'd be willing to give it another try at some point, but this experience really dampened my excitement.

UPDATE: I got the chance to play this a second time, and even with lowered expectations after my first play, I didn't come away with any higher opinion.  This game ended with a closer score (10-5-4), but the ending was abrupt and anti-climactic.  It simply seems that being a merchant is a much easier way to win than through pirating.  Getting glory both for trading in three in-demand goods, along with the money from the trade, seem to be much more efficient than raiding merchant ships, with less risk involved.  While I suppose I'd be willing to play this on occasion, I can't imagine myself asking to play it.  My rating of a 6 will stand.

+Lots of gameplay options.
+Great job of capturing the theme.
+Awesome plastic ships.
+Allows for both peaceful (merchant) and aggressive (marauder) strategies.
+Well-designed player aids.

-High degree of randomness can lead to a runaway leader.
-Lots of downtime, especially when opponents take a porting action and you do not.
-Many of the ship upgrades are geared towards combat, which seems to be a relatively minor part of the game (at least in my one play).
-Some fiddly rules (e.g. special weapons, harbor rules, crew combat).
-Merchant strategy much more effective than marauder strategy.
-Anti-climactic end game.

RATING: 6
I so want to love this game...

Pros:
- pirates!
- beautiful board and components
- multiple ways to earn points and multiple paths to victory but only if playing with aggressive players
- nice thematic touches with rumour cards and missions
- the sense of dread when NPCs or other players are coming for you and you are holding a full load of great cargo (but again only if other players are aggressive)

Cons:
- absolutely need the right group of players (aggressive, tactically minded, prone to quick analyses, and fun)
- sometimes has very low decision making and too much time between turns leading to a feeling of a slow playing game (this is particularly frustrating for me)
- playing the merchant can become very boring if the pirates are not aggressive, as the pick up and deliver aspect has little decision making in itself

RATING: 8.1
I really like this game, and it is perfect for a Saturday game day with 2-3 other people.  It takes a good 3-4 hours, but all that time is spent having a great time.  It has been said by others, but it is so true, you need to pressure people to be ready for their turns and take them in a reasonable amount of time.  I don't get it. I can almost always get through my turns in a minute or two, sometimes just 20 seconds.  But others can take FOREVER.  Sell, Buy, Fix your ship, get event, hear rumor, recruit crew.  That's it.  It does not need to take forever, and if you let people sit there take their time, the game will not end.

All that said.  If people will just resolve to be ready for their turns and take them, this game is an absolute blast.  It is so much more fun to be a pirate.  I don't care how much better it is points wise to be a merchant.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.85
The most well-themed game I have ever played! "Dripping" with theme? Nahhh: we had to use bath towels afterwards to wipe up the table! Extremely well-themed; and historically accurate, too! That's why it's a hard job being a pirate in M&M: historically, it was a challenge to be a successful pirate.
Be warned: your first game or two will seem dreadfully long. But it's amazing how quickly the length of a game of M&M shortens with subsequent plays.
You will also find the rules to be exceedingly fiddly. That's only because they are! BUT: a few plays will get you used to the system. And for those of us whose birth certificate indicates a certain unfortunate fact, the font size on the cards (and to a lesser extent the board) might be a "little" annoying!
Once you get past that, though, you have an outstanding game of risk management that is also well themed. Many people here have lamented the huge luck factor in the game, and there is a HUUUGE amount of luck. But the key to the game is how do I manage the gobs of luck? You have to learn when to take risks, and when to avoid them like scurvy. And that ain't easy, since there are so many options to choose from. Some of those options are very good for pirates; some of them are very bad. Some are very good for merchants; some are very bad. I think merchants do have the advantage, generally, but an average merchant, in my opinion, will NOT be able to win against a clever pirate. The first thing a pirate has to do is to accept the fact that he's going to be beaten up a lot, and focus not only on risk management, but on loss management as well. For example: a pirate losing his sloop is not (necessarily) a disaster; a pirate losing his frigate IS!!!
I suspect I may not want to play M&M with AP prone players, however: there is an awful lot to consider in most turns!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
  I love this game, be a pirate and roam the seas as a scurvy villain, or peacefully hop from port to port as a wholesome merchant, or maybe a bit of both.

  The idea of the game as either role is to accrue gold and glory. Get both from either selling goods that are in demand at ports or heading out to sea to raid merchant vessels and sink other ships.

  The game plays very well but has a little too much down time and many people find the combat mechanics clunky... I put this down to a lack of imagination; if you can well imagine how a sea battle will play out from the moment you spot an enemy ship, then you should be able to grasp why the combat works how it does, if you don't, then you'll be rolling dice with no idea why.

  The artwork is beautiful and the rumour and mission cards really get you into the role of your captain. There is a lot to keep track of but at the end of the day, it's a fairly easy game to pick up. Yahaarrrr me hearties, this be gettin 9 dubloons!

  P.S.. Don't get too attached to your captain if you are a pirate, he will die eventually.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Includes:
[thing=161167][/thing]

:arrowE: [u]Synopsis[/u]:
A so-called "sandbox" adventure game saddled somewhere between smooth Euro mechanics, daring dice fests, and press-your-luck. Intrigue, flavor text, supply and demand, lots of ship stat customization, smart NPC AI for multiple factions, tremendous artwork, interesting plot in missions and rumors, high risk-versus-reward gameplay, set collection, emergent alliances, lots of variable action spots, with very thematic combat dice-based combat and choose-your-own-adventure style paths to victory.

:arrowE: [u]What I like most[/u]:
The narrative is amazing in this game. Even playing it with the goal of sheer points optimization, a player cannot ignore the story that develops as his or her captain embarks into the sea with their strengths and weaknesses in tow, slowly changing as rumors, missions, close-calls, raids, epic sales, dramatic events, and rowdy player interaction all mingle together into something much greater than the sum of its parts. I once had a crappy sloop which was able to raid and capture a frigate from the Royal English navy by calling in the help of a nearby privateer captain. Between the captain's crew and my guns, the huge frigate was slowly whittled down to a single crew member, and my crew was able to prevail on the final die roll...!

:arrowE: [u]What I like least[/u]:
There is a great deal of strategy and mitigation in this game, but some aspects are definitely boiled down to luck. Granted, I usually play a Marauder, which is inherently more press-your-luck than the steady consistency of playing as a Merchant... :whistle::arrrh:

[hr]
As a glimpse into the tremendous world of this game, I'll describe a single session which had a spectacular interaction:

I was able to claim a mission called "Joined Forces" which allowed me, as a marauder in a lowly sloop, to engage an English frigate in St. John... with the help of the pirate sloop NPC on the board. Basically, I rolled for the pirate sloop and my friend rolled for the frigate... it was a deathmatch and we ended up killing all of each other's crew in the same final roll. Since the frigate had more successes in the roll, he "won" and the pirate sloop was destroyed (R.I.P. "Long Ben Avery")... at which point MY ship got to join the combat, and I boarded the crew-less frigate in a single roll and claimed it for myself. From there, I ended the game when a Spanish frigate populated in Havana where I was sitting out to sea. I engaged it once it scouted me and I sunk that sucker to the bottom of the ocean for my final necessary glory point.

[hr]
:arrowE: [size=13][url=https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLYOW-vlXZtjNWQm8zT5Ppe04qRiW5jQlj][b]PLAYLIST[/b][/url][/size]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.9
It seems to take too long, and there's so much to keep track of.  I don't remember another game where we had to flip through the rulebook so much.  What's worse, I actually found myself not wanting to finish the game, which hasn't happened in quite some time.  We actually agreed to quit before we finished.  This game seems great in concept, but there's just too much going on.  I wonder, however, if this might change with greater familiarity of the rules.  I could see my rating of this game moving up a point after future plays.  There were some things I liked.  For example, I like how the combat works, where each player announces 1 of 3 combat tactics, and then rolls for Seamanship to determine who gets to execute their tactic.  The theme is also ever-present throughout the game, and the components are very good.  Unfortunately, game play seems too tedious (at the moment, at least).

RATING: 8
Rating based on one play.

I've been disappointed with a lot of the latest big theme games, but this was an exception.  It's nicely produced and designed and the best part is how there are so many ways to score.  

You can act as a merchant and move goods around, go pirate and steal from NPCs and other players, or focus on completing missions and investigating rumors.  And really, you'll probably focus on several things at the same time.  

The piracy system offers some nice trade-offs. You can score big and possibly slow down another player, but the bounties placed on your head restrict your options elsewhere.

One complaint might be that the game finished just as it felt like it was getting started.  A few of us had just built larger ships, some navy ships had arrived on the board, but we hadn't yet done any ship to ship combat.  We could have increased the Glory Point requirement, but it had already been a few hours.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

If another player kills you they take everything you have. Everything! But isn't that the life of a pirate?

RATING: 7
NOTE: Game might have changed from prototype!

Impressions after two games:

Overall: Fun!
Manages to capture the feel of sailing the seas, of pirating and trading very well. Lots of theme, lots of cards with texts on them, lots of dice, too. 

Risk-taking is a big part of the game, and it can be really nasty: Storms force you around, wars prevent you from trading where you wanted to, and of course, big baddy Blackbeard had to attack you, of all ships.

However, bad things happen to everyone (there's a whole lot of fun watching the trouble of other players), and even after a series of bad rolls and card draws, or after dying three times (as I did in my second game), you might still win in the end.

Even so, if you can't live with temporary (random) setbacks, the game is probably not for you.

The game mechanics are simultaneous action selection (which direction am I going to sail? Or would I rather go to port, scout for ships to combat, or try to follow another ship?), commodity demand by randomly drawing chits, random events from a card deck, and rumor cards that the players draw.

You have lots to do and decide. Am I going to be pirate or trader? Am I going to pursue a rumor, or rather try to make money by trading or sinking merchant ships? Should I upgrade the ship I have, or rather save the money for a better ship? And so on.

I'd love to play it again...

UPDATE:
Published version, played one two-player and one three-player game. Although some rules have changed, the feel of the game is still the same, and I see my current rating confirmed.

UPDATE 2:
The game did lose some flavor as compared to the beta version, but it plays a lot shorter.
Luck can be a massive factor. The fact that now players can turtle from harbor to harbor means that in some cases, lucky players are hard to attack, and therefore can reach their 10 glory points rather quickly.

RATING: 6.5
First play: thematically very strong.  Very similar to the computer game, "Sid Mier's Pirates!". I think fans of the genre and games like "Arkham Horror" or "Tales of Arabian Nights" will really enjoy this title.  (I think I like M&M better than both those two).  

The game itself suffers from a lot of the problems that "thematic games" can have.  I found the game play somewhat underwhelming.  The choices somewhat dull. Downtime (espcially with 4 new players) was also an issue.

On the other hand, Merchants and Marauders offers up a pretty solid "pirate experience", and while the choices in the game aren't thrilling, you do feel a certain amount of freedom.  There's definitly room in this game for "play".

I dont think I'll be buying this game but I certainly wouldnt mind playing it again.

RATING: 10
Awesome components, great stuff. High quality production. This game has quite some rules to remember, takes some time to play and is somewhat heavy.
The only complaint I have is depending on the Captain that's randomly assign to you, you're more suited to either being a pirate or a merchant, because if you try to be a pirate with a captain that is very weak at seamanship you'll lose badly. Yeah you can still raid merchants and win (mostly because of special weapons), but fighting other player pirates... forget it.
I'll probably fix that by drawing only captains with the same seamanship level, 3 would be a good number. (So you can have a chance against naval ships).
Otherwise this is a very dense game and there's lots of good things going for it. You can do pretty much what a pirate would do - trade goods, fight other captains, and possibly plunder their ships, go and search for certain rumors to be true, doing all sort of missions, claim bounties, upgrade your ship, buy different ships depending on your play style and your Captain stats.
If you want a heavy and deep pirate game this is probably the one to get. But it only goes up to 4 players.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This is a 3 hour race game with injections of theme and randomization. It manages to be a fun experience. Each session provides a sense of danger as you maraud the seas or legally peddle your cargo at the various ports. The naval ships and pirate ships, when they are present, add to the danger. The individual turns, with a few exceptions, move pretty quickly so the game can handle four people pretty well (at least as compared to Xia). If the players aren't confrontational with each other, the game seems to come down to the success on some dice rolls. If the players are very confrontational with each other, the game can go on a bit longer than it probably should.  Under the base game rules, you have to keep an eye on a merchant who's managed to collect 50 gold, as that can quickly determine the game.

The expansion adds a lot of modules that allow the players to tune the game to their preferences. It's good, but not mandatory.

Edit: the battle resolution is too long and procedural for this sort of game. Really detracts from the marauder play style. Heck, the marauder style feels pretty poor overall compared to the simplicity of the merchant play style.

Merchants & Marauders: Seas of Glory (2015)
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A board game version of "Sid Meirer's Pirates." This is an "experience" game that allows players to tell their own stories based on the choices they make. There is a winner and a looser, but if you have the right mindset you can have so much fun making up your own adventures that it doesn't always matter. It can be a bit long, but there are some designer created house rules to speed things up. One of my favorite games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Most people would look at my 10 star rating with a very critical eye, but allow me the chance to explain myself!  At the time of this review I have logged 15 plays of M&M, and this is STILL my favorite game; I am always itching to play it, and I can't foresee it ever growing stale for me. There's just too much to do! Too much fun to be had! 

M&M is a sandbox Ameritrash game, and it excels at both those things. There are a great variety of strategies to employ, and they are all viable routes to victory. And for this reason, M&M does a fantastic job of emulating the feeling of being a pirate. It's also juuuuust trashy enough to introduce a random, chaotic component, but isn't so punishing that you can't recover from a small disaster (which probably will happen). There are lots of ways to mitigate disaster, but you won't always have the resources to invest in them. 

M&M is the best pirate game to date, but I recognize this game won't work for every person. If you like the golden age of piracy, sandbox-style games, and don't mind chucking dice every now and then, I urge you to give this game a try. I would also advise picking up the modular expansion, because it's very easy to incorporate and adds some fantastic new mechanics.

RATING: 7
First impression after one play:

+ Superb theme and superb conversion. No paste-up here.
+ Though complex, the rules are easy to understand and the rulebook is very clear.
+ Multiple paths to victory, with equal chanes but a completely different gaming experience. 
+ Great components
+ Great Narration
+ No Player Elimination

- Downtime heavy
- Low (mostly indirect) Player interaction
- Attacking other players has 50:50 odds (even when Pirates attack Merchants), so should be avoided

RATING: 7
OK, quite a nice game, very piratey, but not a lot to distinguish this one from many other pirate games - Plunder for example, or Pirate's Cove.

All the same mechanisms are there, the race to get a bigger or better ship, the large amounts of luck in finding a ship to plunder (and in what you find) or in dodging various navies.

In fact, this one reminds me very closely of plunder in many ways.

So all in all, OK game but nothing new.

RATING: 7
An okay pirate game, but I think there is a bit too much luck for my liking... and the pirate and NPC navies can make the game harsh if certain event cards come out together or fail to move these big-bad ships.  The combat takes too long.  That said, I'm anxious to play again to figure out how to play this game more competitively... I just floundered in last place trying to be a trade ship but failing to get cheap goods (3-of-a-kind or better).

Note to self:  you really must play this like Vinci or Small World... just kill off your pirate as soon as things are looking grim... if you're down to 4 safe spaces on the board, nail some merchant ships for a quick glory point or two and let the big-bad navies kill you so you can do it all over again.

RATING: 8
This has been a big hit with the kids although it can be brutal when you get attacked and lose your ship. The gameplay is tremendous fun be you merchant or pirate and there are plenty of interesting choices throughout the game. There is a fairly high level of randomness but experience and strategy can help mitigate this. The game looks beautiful with great components. The rulebook was hard to flick through for reference purposes but after a couple of plays you get the rules down and the game flows smoothly. We found that provided players are focused on gaining glory points, the game-length is a reasonably 2 hours or so for 4 players. Games could go longer if players are too timid to go for glory.

This ones borderline a 9 rating for the fun game-play. Randomness and some confusing wording on some cards / edge-cases pull it down a point. I'm thinking about the expansion now...

RATING: 8
Fairly impressed after one play. Three of us played with myself and one other choosing to start off as Merchants owing to our Captain draw. The third player drew a Captain that looked to make a decent pirate Captain and he showed how viable that route is to victory. He had read up on the game more than either of us and it showed although this was the first play for all of us. He had his victory conditions about the time the game was just getting going for us. Luck was kind to him no doubt but everything he did made sense and it all worked out golden for him. I'd like to play this game some more and am motivated to do so, which is a good sign. Some of what I've read though suggests it might wear out its welcome after you've explored the game some. Some of the doubts involve the complicated combat system which we didn't see at all so that will be important to try out. Time will tell but so far we like this a lot better than either Pirate Cove or Blackbeard...
++++++
Couple of plays in now and I'm really appreciating the game's design. Fairly straight-forward but with interesting subtleties and decision points. The combat system needs to be studied carefully but is solid once you become familiar with it. This has easily become my favorite "pirate-themed" game - much better than the simpler "Pirate's Cove" and miles ahead of "Blackbeard."
++++++
More play and a bit of a pattern seems to be emerging - if you get lucky with trade goods, rumours and/or missions, you may well find yourself within reach of a quick win while others are still trying to upgrade their boats. This has happened to us twice now and the game is suddenly over just as you felt you were getting going. There may be a way to tweak the victory conditions to give the game more of a "mid-phase" but I'm not yet sure (other than just upping the VP requirement) how to go about it...

RATING: 7
The quintessential pirate game! Has an awesome amount of choices and various routes to victory. The components are terrific and the gameplay is fun. DO NOT play with anyone prone to AP as it will make the game drag and will cause your friends to hate it. It is an ameritrash game and has quite a bit of luck involved.

The life of a pirate is tough and the naval ships do not play around. Its probably best to be a merchant for a few turns and purchase a better ship or a few upgrades before starting your life of piracy.

Overall, I really like this game and I think the next time I play I will enjoy it even more!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Captures the feeling of Sid Meier's C64 classic very well.
I like the different mechanisms for trading, capturing merchantmen and ship fights as well as the story telling in the missions and rumours and the background as a whole. 
However, the game depends rather heavily on the players to add drama and suspense, as it could be played in a rather solitary style, too.
In our games, the best moments were ship fights, that can mostly be avoided by unaggressive players.
At least in the first games, port actions can drag a little, although we tried to keep things going.

RATING: 9

And therein lies the beauty of the game, between all of the luck based events (event cards, glory cards, cargo cards, dice rolls for combat, rumour cards... you get my point) and the 'open world' style of the game - no tactic is superior as your opponents can always find a way to mess you up if they so choose!

RATING: 4
Well now, this is a tough one to rate.   I guess I've been spoiled by Sid Meier's Pirates! (the PC game) from which M&M is clearly derived.     The problem is that this game is just so slow and poorly paced compared to the PC game.

Let's start with the components... this is a beautifully constructed game.  Everything is polished and even the relatively lengthy rules are for the mostpart straightforward.

However...

Merchants appear to have a fairly boring existence, effectively playing an Empire Builder mini-game without drawing tracks.   Pirates are a little more interesting, but the balance certainly doesn't favor them.

Downtime is also a bit of a problem in that turns range anywhere between 3 seconds and 5 minutes, as a whole range of port actions are executed.

So, while I can understand that the theme appeals to some people, this feels like an inferior reproduction of a fantastic computer game.  The boardgame really needs a CPU to handle the movement of NPC ships, battle rolls, etc.   So get the computer game!

I'd like to point out that the designer of this game is incredibly helpful to people on the BGG forums.  That alone deserves some credit, and it's nice to see that a designer cares to participate like that.  

Still, this is not a game for me and the people I game with.

RATING: 9
A solid game with plenty of fun for everyone! The game really sucks you into its atmosphere. Playing a pirate is a lot harder than one might expect, but the rewards can be huge if you manage to pull it off. As such, it is quite realistic and deciding which risks are worth taking is key to this game!

The only thing I do not appreciate is the random selection of a captain. If you do not feel confident to play a pirate, you may end up with a pirate captain that has but little advantages to offer to a merchant player. Alternatively, you can just try your luck OR retire your captain, although both could cost you (either money or a turn).

The components are high-quality although the reference sheets are a bit large. Knowing the sea zone advantages by heart really helps, so you tend to become better at this game over time for this reason alone.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Love this game! Had my eye on it for over a year, but hesitated because of the price tag, but glad I finally shelled out the cash.. it's great player interaction, engaging, and it has pirates! Beautiful art, good pieces, and the box is like a brick! Full of great stuff.

Definitely the best pirate game I have played so far, even over Pirates' Cove. If you enjoy pirate-themed games, this one will scratch your itch.. it carries the theme throughout the game, from the ship miniatures you get to move around the Caribbean map board to the stories on mission and rumor cards. Sailing the seas and exploring new ports, scouting and raiding merchant ships for cargo, following rumors, hunting down pirates for bounties and fighting naval ships out to bring you to justice all add to the rousing feel that you are really a pirate captain in the old Caribbean, sailing for gold and glory!

The random element of event, glory, mission, and rumor cards that come out keep the game very interesting, and the dice keep you on the edge of your seat when fighting a naval captain with a faster ship or more cannon. It also gives you a chance at a dramatic victory (think critical hit for role-players out there) when the odds are against you. One very cool aspect of the game is the different captains available to each player, each featuring different stats on their corresponding captain cards - each has a unique ability that gives them an edge over others in certain areas of the game, and some are better suited for pirating while others make better merchants. The only complaint I have in this regard is that some captains are clearly more dominant than others, where they possess greater skill in seamanship, for example, and are therefore guaranteed to be much more successful pirates, as this is the most crucial skill for piracy in the game. There are ways to overcome this discrepancy, however, and the game is still fun despite the fact. The rules tell each player to draw a captain randomly, but we allow each player to choose from two cards, so to give them a bit more control over determining their role in the game. The pirate captain profiles combined with rolling for attacks in battles and "leveling up" your ship gives this game a great role-playing element that will make you feel like you're in an RPG with a unique character to play.

Of course, I should also mention that you can trade your way to victory as well; hence the word "merchants" in the game title. This turns out to be a potentially far more lucrative role in the game, if merchants are left alone by other players who opt toward piracy. This creates a necessity for players to be naturally at odds, which makes the game more exciting, but makes it a little more determined as well: pirate players must attack merchant players, or they will be allowed to amass wealth too easily; yet, all of a player's wealth is transferred to another if he is defeated in battle, so the power differential created can be a problem going forward in the game. As long as you know this going in, and can plan for it, and not get upset at the game or players, you'll be alright.

The major drawback of the game is the downtime between turns - each player typically has a lot to do on his turn, so each other has to wait a while. Our gaming group just passes around multiplayer iPad games during most of our sessions anyway, so there's no downtime for us - problem solved!

If you're looking for rich and robust themed gaming experience with lots of interaction, decision-making, high-stakes chance, and role-playing elements that lasts about 2 hours - and you love pirates - this is definitely your game.

RATING: 8.25
This is a game I wanted to love, but ended up just liking quite a bit.

On the plus side, the game does give you a good sense of trading, sailing and pirating in a certain age.  It seems like fun to be a pirate until you realize everyone wants to turn you in!  The game has lots of detail and tries to add atmosphere through the mission and rumor cards.  Great components, with a particularly lovely board.

The real issue here is downtime - with 4 players, AP from one person can make it an eternity until another player needs to pay attention (cue the smartphones being whipped out).  Also we found that until one player decided to go the pirate route, it lacked excitement.

Unlike most games, this time I'm anxious to try it with less players, as I think it might tighten things up and make it more interesting.  But on the whole I'm intrigued and anxious to play it again.

RATING: 7
I really liked, and enjoyed, the theme in this game!  You really do feel like a merchant, or a pirate (if you choose), when playing this game. The realism comes from playing the rumour, mission, and glory cards.  It is fun to try to fulfill a mission, or venture to see whether a rumour is true (am I lucky enough to roll the influence I need?).  There is a certain push your luck portion to this game (Do I roll the dice to attack one more time?; do I dare pick up another cargo card in a merchant raid?; do I have enough to be successful?). This level of tension, the cool map, and awesome models, make this game fun and worth its adventure.

On the negative side, this game feels like there is a little too much luck (ex. dice rolling, random enemy ship placement, etc.) and the game is just way too long (It took me over 4 hours to play it).  The rules are not the easiest to learn; there are a lot of rules - and combat felt somewhat convoluted.  

On the positive, the game feels fun and I want to play it again! Sadly, I am not sure when I will ever get it back to the table (especially with more than 2 players).

RATING: 5
Played three times. Did not really enjoy much. Game is very, very long -- particularly for a dice-fest!

The theme is great; the components are great.

The randomness is crippling... you can take credit for very little of your success and you have no real need to take blame for your failures, either. (And it's not just dice randomness, but the cards, too. I don't like winning or losing a 3-4 hour game based almost entirely on getting better cards or better rolls.)

Setup and takedown time are pretty big.

Downtime, a myriad of different rules that frequently aren't all that intuitive...

Too much hype on this one. Wow.

RATING: 8
Excellent, medium-light pirate game. Pretty much what [i]Blackbeard[/i] wanted to be but absolutely failed at. This should be your pirate game of choice if you're looking for something in the medium complexity range.

I do think the game could use some variation in terms of how points are scored. Some fan based variants posted here are worthy of consideration, especially the ones that limit how many VP you can score simply by stashing cash.

Also, not all captains are created equal, but a simple house rule of drawing two and picking one usually resolves that.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Merchant & Marauders is a cross between a Euro game and a thematic Ameritrash game where you play the role of a ship captain.  As a ship captain, you can either buy and sell goods as a merchant, or become a pirate (or a combination of the two).

I'm very conflicted about this game.  On the one hand, the high quality components and great core game play make for a very compelling theme with interesting decisions.  But there are a hundred annoying rule exceptions added on top of the core rules that make learning the game a horrendously unpleasant experience.  Many of these fiddly rule exceptions only come into play once every 3 or 4 games, but players are constantly forced to read the exceptions to figure out if they are relevant.  In my first game of M&M, I received 6 Glory cards and 2 Rumor cards, each with 5 - 10 sentences of text.  But after wading through the text, while trying to follow the game play, it became evident that only 2 of the cards could have become relevant to the game play.  In the end, not one of these 8 cards affected game play to ANY extent.  All they did was pull my attention away from the fun game play experience, and waste my time.  Further compounding the problem is that the icons on the cards are not perfectly consistent nor intuitive.

Another one of my complaints is that there are several different types of combat rules that are not consistent.  For instance, there are different rules for fighting a NPC merchant ship and for fighting a player merchant ship.  There are different rules if one of the ships opts to board, and different rules if the combat takes place with a warship instead of an armed pirate ship, etc.

The theme and the core game mechanics get an 8 or a 9.  I REALLY like them.  The fiddly rule exceptions and the other mechanics which are not core (meaning they don't come up very often) get a 2 or a 3.  So in the end, I have rated this game a 5.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
Rating could rise with subsequent plays.  First game was too frenetic for me and was difficult to enjoy/understand.  We played where players took their turns without waiting for previous player to finish.  This led to me not fully understanding what I could do in the game.  I had no idea what the other players were doing either. I couldn't really watch them take their turns to learn.   The rating was also hurt because we had to skip a lot of the game explanation because one of the players ran out of patience with the rules.  Ironically he was the same fellow who kept interrupting the game explanation for strategy questions.

However, even if I had gotten all the rules and/or could learn the game better from observing others during their turn, it still felt one-dimensional to me.  I was a merchant and I know there was more to the game (fighting) than what I was doing.  But the merchant dimension felt like a very simple pick up and delivery game.  Try to get 3 of a kind, deliver for glory points and accumulate 50 bucks.  Realized after the game, that I could of thrown in a couple of missions/rumors for some extra points.  I think there is more here to like, but until I get an idea of what that may be, I have to leave it at 5...a take it or leave it game.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Players represent a captain running a ship around the Caribbean.  They can be nice and lawful, trying to eek a living from honest merchant trade, or turn pirate and aim for fast wealth.  Lavish, lovely looking game.  Players take turns to take three actions - sail, scout or port.  Sailing is simply moving, but may barge into trouble from the navies of the world.  Scouting is how to find merchants and such.  Port actions involve honest trade, refit and upgrades to your ships.  Nice, playable game that is very reminiscent of Avalon Hill's Blackbeard (about 10 similar mechanics/ideas, but it is a coincidence, apparently).  A four player game, each racing to 10 glory points, is going to take a long time, and the action is interrupted too often by the long port actions of the players, as well as a laborious multi-step combat system.  I can see the appeal, but Avalon Hill's Blackbeard's blindingly fast action/turns, and tense uncertainty, make that game so much more appealing, and it's faster and more historical too.  This one feels like a 15 year old game that missed the flute with modern, interactive game mechanics.  Two plays were enough to convince me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Fun, and captures well the feel of Sid Meier's Pirates!, which I love.

Many of the mechanisms (e.g. trading) feel way too light for the game length. Or, alternatively, the game is way too long for its weight. Just not satisfying for such a long play time.

I really hate it when a player is severely weakened by the game, then defeated by another player, who reaps an undue reward. This definitely happens in this game.

RATING: 8
This game is simply awesome!  If you like theme and immersion and pirates - then this game is for you!  Playing as a Merchant or a Pirate makes no difference - this game is fun as hell either way!  Aaaargh! :arrrh:

M&M works very well solitaire with some very simple adjustments.  Not sure why a solitaire mode is not included in the box.  These game designers and publishers really need to start understanding how important solo rules are!  I knocked my rating a bit because of this.

Regardless, if an official co-op version ever appeared, I would rate this game higher.

Also, the wife loves this one!  :cool:

RATING: 8
One of the more controversial games in my collection, well at least in my game group.  I would call this the game that Blackbeard should have been.  It has all the elements of trading and piracy that people want in a pirate game and it can be played fairly quickly.  Now I would agree that there is definitely a bit of downtime and it might not work for more than two or three players.  I would also agree that it seems too easy for those taking the merchant route to win but I think overall it does a great job of combining a pirate game and a trading game into a single package.  I need to play this game more and see if piracy can be successful. Update: 2015 - Rekindled my interest in this game by taking a look at a solo variant I found online and it works great.  Definitely need to explore that variant more.

RATING: 8.5
This is a blast.  One of my favourite thematic games.  Don't be put off by the 4-hour run time.  Just choose a bunch of pals who're patient, not too AP-prone, and, ideally, don't mind screwage or life not turning out fair.

I think it's important that people are enjoying the conversation at the table in this game, because it's quite possible someone will be effectively eliminated from the game (by repeated defeat) quite early on, and there are no significant catch-up mechanisms that I'm aware of.    (Alternatively. It won't break the game if that player leaves the table, though it might break your heart).

You can play as aggressively or as independently as you think will fit the group - there's plenty game in either direction.  Lovely and thematic, all the rules make sense, so if your group is forgiving, you can actually have them start immediately, and teach the game during that first play (perhaps with the two advisories that 1) ship upgrades don't regen, and that 2) selling three of the same in-demand cargo is MUCH stronger than selling two).

Very pretty on the table.

I lost my first game by miles, still had great fun!

This opinion is after 2 long, fun games (one was with some modules from Seas of Glory expansion).

RATING: 7
Thematically this game is an ace in the whole, and reminds me a lot of the Sid Meier's Pirates! video game series, except its you instead of the game that is keeping track of your stats, reputation, and other important information.  The amount of things you can do is really incredible, and a little intimating, though I respect and enjoy the amount of freedom each player is given to figure out how to succeed in their chosen profession, and ultimately achieve victory.  However, some of the gameplay elements don't seem very fleshed out, and there can be a LOT of downtime between players, with little to do except plan your next move.  The game probably needs some tweaking and house rules to get the most out of it, and the right group of people.  Highly recommended for people who love the theme, or thematic games at all.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Z-Man/2011
The theme is carried out exceedingly well and pleasingly accurate.  For instance, combat is complicated but unique, involving maneuvering of the ships, combat shots, boarding followed by crew combat.  

Components: Excellent plastic ships and large, two-sided player aids (rules says 2 included, but my box had 4). Massive text on cards. Good player boards and very large treasure chests.  The rules are well written and not difficult (battle being the most complicated), but it took me hours to go over the rules because there are so many facets to remember, and forgetting one thing could greatly change the play of the game.  Once play started, I was pleased how everything fell into place. 

You can modify ships in numerous ways, upgrade to bigger ships, repair ships, move on the sea or into ports, modify combat, go on missions, prove rumors, buy and sell goods, increase your crew, add specialists, attack or raid, place gold in a safe treasure chest, and more--hence the extended rule reading.

Because conflicts enhance the game, playing with the full 4 players is more alluring to me, because engagements increase.  There are several avenues to gaining Glory Points and winning the game, one of which is through combat, but if only rare or occasional combat occurs, the game seems rather bland.  The game has some built in potential conflict through non-player pirates and navies, that are moved around the board in a unique way.   So even if players don't attack, limited battles should occur anyway, especially as the game progresses and the number of non-player ships enter the board. 

This is the most satisfying pirate game I have played.  The reason it didn't get higher than a 6, is because I will have to spend an hour or more reviewing the rules before each play or play it often, either of which is hard to do with a game that then lasts 3 hours and needs four to play.

RATING: 7
Beautifully produced, but I am still undecided as to the different ways of winning at this game.  Both games I have tried focused around Merchants simply hoarding and building up glory through 3 desired goods trades.  I tried my hand at being a pirate but once the Naval ships start roaming all possible corners of the sea, you are extrememly limited in options.  It seems this game has two reliable paths to victory: a blitz pirate victory before the big ships come out, or a drawn-out merchant victory which is principally based around drawing the right kind of goods for the closest ports.  Both games I played saw a victory through the latter option.

I will play again and probably try my hand at being a pirate but that depends on the starting captain.  So my choice will also be based on a random draw...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
All 4 players were new to the game.  Took a little while to get going with learning the rules, but after the first few initial rounds things started rolling.  Future plays will go a lot faster since we know what we're doing.

The winner ended up being the guy that used his captain's skill the best and did a lot of Missions/Rumors with a little merchant trading thrown in.  The rest of us tried our hand at piracy but came up short.

Everyone agreed that it was a great game and would play it again.

After a second play, I really like this game.  Key, though, is that you can't play nice and need to go after other players, otherwise you'll have someone stash 50 gold and win.

I would always play with the house rule that you cannot collect more than 2 or 3 Glory points from stashed gold since that stashed gold almost always makes up half the winning pirates gold.

If there are any problems with it, it's the combat rules where you're rolling dice and depending on what each player decided to do only some dice are used and you can't run if the other player tried to board, etc.  It needed a whole flowchart.

2/2017 - had to bump this out of a 10 slot as I haven't played it recently and it is difficult to get to the table.

Donated to Gaming Hoopla library.

RATING: 6
Pirates in the Caribbean! The success of a game like this hinges on theme integration. The mechanics are solid, although players need to deal with a fair share of randomness but where the game really shines is thematic density.

The transfer of the Golden Age of Piracy to the table works pretty well. Many of the usual pirate clichés translate directly to game elements. The biggest issues with the game are downtime and the low player interaction. Other players are the only real threat to players (NPC naval ships and pirates can be tough but are usually easily avoided; NPC merchant vessels are (too) easy prey) no matter if they earn their money as traders or pirates but the incentives to actually attack other players are pretty much non-existent. In most cases, the odds are roughly 50:50 so you'd much rather plunder another helpless merchant or seal another glorious trade instead.

Mechanically, the game is pretty uninspired. Neither the merchants nor the pirates have particuoarly tough decisions to make, and drawing the right cards or rolling successes at the right moment go a long way to victory.

RATING: 7
It's a gorgeous game that is entirely about creating a pirate story. It is thematically brilliant, albeit complicated, but the stories leave me unsatisfied, ultimately. There is an obscenely high risk to reward correlation. I don't mind this normally, but being a contendor ultimately can come down to a single die roll (or a terrible global event card). If someone goes for that goal, they can either put themselves in a near untouchable place (requiring higher risks on the parts of other players to catch up), or remove them as a serious comeptitor in the game. As a story telling mechanism, this game is fabulous and requires very little imagination to immerse yourself. If you play this game with the primary intention of winning, however, walk away. It is too easy to crash on the shore and get torn to pieces just based on the roll of the dice.

RATING: 7
M&M is an amazing game and does a nice job of balancing mechanics and theme.  The theme is wonderfully realized and the mechanics have just enough strategy and luck in them to not get too much in the way of the theme.  Yes, there are some events that can heavily flip a player's advantage and some things can come down to lucky dice rolls and chance card pulls, but the theme is mostly served by these design choices. Most times with games likes these I feel the mechanics suffer to prop up the theme. This simply isn't the case for M&M, where you feel at the very least at the helm of any randomness. This is largely due to a tightly constructed game system and enough moving parts that allow you to manipulate the luck to some advantage. I put this game in the top category of theme-heavy games. This is how it should be done.  Unfortunately, it's a chore and headache to teach and the theme can get buried in some muddy design. It is hard to find a first-time player who doesn't get buried under the sandbox style of the game. Also, it's difficult to even play this game casually and only getting to play this game once a year or so I feel robs me of an experience where the game should really flow.  And there's no denying that the buying and selling of goods is the most boring part of the game and it's a pretty significant part (for a merchant, anyway). Overall, I'm impressed in this games design and approach and it deserves the praise it gets, even if it's got a couple of ugly (but mostly unavoidable) warts.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
If you had the fortune to play Sid Meier's Pirates back in the days of the Commodore '64, then this game will recreate that experience for you, but with 3 OTHER PLAYERS!
This game has experienced more repeat "table time" after purchase than any other game I own (except Dominion.)
The theme works very well, especially if you are willing to "go pirate" enough to attack your friends. 
And you should. I mean it. 
Go full-on Pirate.
I'll explain in a moment.

The game slowly introduces new elements and becomes more complex as you play, and EVERY CHOICE can lead to victory or demise. 
The only complaints I have with the game are: experienced players have a HUGE advantage over new ones, and once someone gets in the lead, they are very hard to catch. 
A caveat here though- that's the idea.
 
If some fancy-pants merchant starts burning up the glory track to victory, you and your fellow marauders should TAKE HIM DOWN!
The game wants you to fight each other, and you should, otherwise it gets unbalanced quickly. Once you get past your timid nature and start blasting each other right in the timbers, things get more even-keeled.

This game has great theme, great components (even though the ships beg for a nice paint job), and it gets pirates, and the changing winds of fortune on the Caribbean absolutely right.
My only other mild criticism is that the end-game can be anti-climatic, but that's only because you haven't been paying attention to your opponents. They will sneak up on you and win while you're just getting started. Even more reason to keep a broadside ready.

WARNING- don't play with angry gamers, spouses, and or close family members who can't take a proper beating now and again. When someone takes your ship, crew, cargo, upgrades, glory cards, kills your captain and leaves you with NOTHING but a starting vessel and a new character with only 10 gold to spend- it's going to get ugly.
Forget victory.
You'll be plotting REVENGE.

RATING: 6.5
Certainly the best pirate game I've played, and it gets more right than wrong. It's handsomely produced, fun to play, and seems broadly accurate within historical standards. But I found the conclusion anti-climatic, and while I played a merchant the whole time I sympathized with the pirate players, who found it very difficult to bring their merchant opponents to battle. It also seemed far too easy to win as a merchant -- selling big sets earns lots of glory (a glory point for a set of three in a demand port, plus it earns you eighteen gold, which is practically enough to purchase two more glory at game's end). Should you really be able to secure nearly a third of the victory points required for a win by selling a big boatload of bananas? Yes, there is a cap on how much glory you can earn through stashing gold, and yes you have to get back to your home port to make that stash ... but I was still able to win in a walk by sailing around the eastern end of the map, assembling four big scores, and buying a ship. It was pleasant enough and I like the theme and so would play again if asked -- a good game but short of great.

RATING: 5.5
Not as good as I would have hoped.  Too locked into a path determined by the pirate you draw.  No way to improve your skills so your locked into a certain role (Pirate, Merchant, or Quester) from the start of the game.  Too few ships,(only 4) really just a pirate and a merchant ship in two sizes big, or small.  All Ships move the same speed, too slow. Attacking a merchant is a boring exercise with no drama or interesting decisions.  Just draw cards and hope you get lucky.  Same with trading, just drawing cards and hoping for the best.  Rolling for rumors and missions can be brutal.  Miss the roll and you have to take 3 more actions,(That's a whole turn)to take another roll.  Not enough interaction with the Non player ships, they hardly ever move.  Combat system is ok, but convoluted.  Boarding actions are just a dice fest.  All said an average game at best.  Long down times, and little interaction.  Just not allot of game there.  It's too bad, I wanted to like it.  But sadly I prefer Pirates cove, which is also only an ok game.  Where or Where is the pirate board game as good as Sid Meier's Pirates?  It's still waiting to be made.

RATING: 6.7
So far this game has only hit the table once. I was really looking forward to playing this game and it was a bit of a let down. However, I will reserve judgement until I can get a couple more plays in. Update - after second play with new people (1.5 hr set up and explanation, 3.5 hr play with one food break), I can say that I do like this game. I just don't like it that much. It is interesting, because it manages to maintain a moderate level of fun throughout the entire play, but never produces memorable highs. That's a shame, because there is a lot of game in here, and possibly even more theme (I love theme!). The mechanics make sense, but they are clunky. Combat is never as satisfying as it should be (even when I manged to board an opponent and wipe the deck with his crew after being attacked and having my ship mangled, I still felt pretty meh).  The will I, won't I of whether or not to stack a bounty on your captain is one of the best features of the game, but doesn't last. Other than that, the missions and rumors spice things up but don't play into the game enough and are a little shallow. It is a fun game that will probably rarely see play, due to the long time investment and relatively low pay out. Hardly a sound investment on the high seas.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
„A Karib-tenger vándorai”
A Libertalia társas mellett ez a gém biztosan felkelti a kedves kalóz-érzelmű játékosok figyelmét, amelyet egy játék erejéig ki is tudtam próbálni. Mivel a szabálykönyv több órás elfoglaltságot ígér és a beltartalom sem kevés, egy 3 fős játék alatt csak részlegesen tudtam a „vitorlaháztető” alá bekukkantani.
A külalak tetszetős, beltartalom minőségi és erősen nyelvfüggő.
A játékban a Karib-tenger egyik kapitányaként mi szeretnék a környék leghíresebb tengerjárói lenni. Alapvetően kereskedéssel és/vagy kalózkodással, vagy inkább más nemzetek vagonjának újraelosztásával törekszünk hírnevet szerezni.
Kezdetben kis hajónkkal, „megbízható” legénységünkkel és feltörekvő álmainkkal keressük kenyerünket, amíg szert nem teszünk jobb és jobb hajókra és vérszemet kapva már nagy tételben játsszuk a partit.
Amit az ember egy kalóz történetből megismer, mind-mind visszaköszön a játékban: trópusi helyszínek, viharok, hurrikánok, hatalmas csatahajók, idegen kalózok, vérdíj, tengeri csata, fosztogatás, kereskedés, híresztelések, „tuti” küldetések, kincsesládánk feltöltése, árulás, … A témában hiba nincs, beszippantja az embert, ha az hagyja magát.
A kártyák mellett halálfejes kockákkal kísértjük szerencsénket, így ezzel is számolnod kell, ha ezen játék mellé szeretnél leülni.
Alapvetően minden körben egy-egy esemény történik, majd a játékosok sorrendben végrehajtják 3 akciójukat és újabb kör következik. Bárki körében bejelentheti, hogy elérte a 10 győzelmi pontot és azzal meg is nyeri a játékot.
A pozitív oldal mellett számomra legnagyobb csalódást a nagy holtidő jelentette, amíg egy-egy játékos végrehajtja körét. Persze ezt lehet csökkenteni, de egyfajta szenvedést jelentett menet közben (mi lehet 4 játékosnál, ha már 3-nál is fárasztó). Bár a partinkban nem történt meg, de egy-egy kapitány más játékos általi kiiktatása a játék közepétől megpecsételheti annak sorsát, győzni már nem fog, marad a bosszú.
Hogy a címből eredően melyik „életvitel” jobb? Kereskedni, kalózkodni, vagy a kettőt kombinálni? Erre nem tudtam rájönni, de egy ilyen játékban inkább hajlik az ember, hogy felhúzza a fekete lobogót, mint, hogy becsületes kereskedő legyen.

RATING: 8
Horrible. Every victory point is randomly scored. Did you draw 3 of a kind? Then you will score 2 VP almost 3 VP. Did you randomly draw a captain with a high influence? Then you will undoubtedly score several points from rumors. 

Did you draw a captain with only 1 inluence? then you won't be completeing many rumors or missions. Did you fail to draw 3 of a kind? No VP for you.While your opponents are racking up VP, gold and glory cards for randomly drawing cargo cards and/or randomly drawing a captain with a high influence, you could be stuck with a captain with a low influence and poor cargo draws. This snowballs into your opponents getting sexier ships so they can defeat most ships on the seas while you are still in your flute or sloop. 

I am undecided as to whether this game is broken.

[b]Update[/b]: I've stuck with the game. And I've come to enjoy the game for what it is.

[b]Update:[/b] There was a lot of subtlety in the game that was missed on me during my first several plays. With the expansion, this game is easily a 9. Once you work out the kinks, the base game is an 8.

RATING: 6
Preliminary rating after my first game.

Nice thematic feel but the game seems clearly unbalanced in favour of the merchants as they can easily win VP after VP just by trading goods from one port to another without being ever intercepted by the pirates.

OTOH, randomness can truly kill the pirates game if the scouting dice are not gentle or some overwhelming glory cards fall in the merchants hands (i.e. Escort).

All in all, the game has got good potential but it seems underdeveloped. 

>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>>

UPDATE: The game drastically improves with the optional rule for ship interception that makes the merchants' life much harder.

However, I still find some design decisions kind of disappointing. For example, frigates are clearly underpowered when compared with galleons. And the merchant raids are way too abstract and boring. 

Last but not least, it clearly suffers from the smack-the-leader syndrome of many other multiplayer games and can easily evolve into an endless series of battles between players (since the combat winner usually comes out pretty weakened and so becomes an easy prey for the rest).

All in all this is a fun game but there's too much randomness and abstraction for my taste.

RATING: N/A
I had been waiting for this one for some time, having read the rules and pre-ordered several years ago.  I was very happy to see this finally in print.

Z-Man made an excellent job with the components, the ship miniatures are GREAT, and the plastic used is perfect (not too soft, not too brittle, and can be painted!).

This game is brimming with theme, and although I dislike PvP (Player versus Player), it is well done in this game, and doesn't take you out of the running if you lose a fight.

Combat is very thematic, and can be a little long for some, but I find it just right, and enjoy watching the combat unfold.  It can become hilarious to watch two crews going at it in hand to hand combat, or two derelict ships (masts reduced to 0) firing at one another until one of them sinks.

The privateering works well, with the bounty and pirate hunters adding some angst.  It may even be worthwhile for other players to hunt you!!  So you better have some special weapons and/or ship upgrades, or it could be a close fight!

Overall feel reminds me of Sid Meier's Pirates!

Game may appear to be long for some, as there are many rules to follow, but they are all intuitive.  Most if not all questions can be answered with the rules booklet, which is nicely done, and the 4 double sided player aids help too!  Thanks Z-Man!

And no need to worry about replayability, as there are hundreds of cards in this one, and the only deck you will normally go through is the cargo deck.

The only negative side thing I can find was with the counters, which were a tad difficult to punch out.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a game I've been waiting for for 3 years when I heard about/stumbled upon it and it was called "Age of Piracy." I've been hankering for a good pirate game that really captures the flavor and fun of Sid Meier's Pirates (the video game).

Ultimately, the game achieves that goal to a degree. I've played 4 times and would like to continue to play it, but as you alude to, there is some downtime that drags it a bit. I've played 2 player, 3 player, and 4 player and 4 is probably the worst because of the downtime, however there are some neat "the board is too crowded, so you get pushed into interesting situations" that happen that are more infrequent with 2 or 3 players.

The design is really neat and truly captures the "Pirates!" feel that Sid Meier created in the video game. You can take on missions, try and raid merchants, be a merchant, pimp out your ship, fight other pirates/navies, etc. All of these really contribute to what I would define as an "experience" rather than a great game. When your small sloop gets into a ship to ship battle with a Man-o-war, you're really fighting to stay alive and maybe you narrowly escape. A great story can be told and I think that's more of the point of the game than to show off elegant mechanics with a pasted-on theme.

There are some interesting variants that add some difficulty to the game that I'd like to try, too. As there are some that make the 2 and 3 player game more "crowded" by increasing the search radius of the NPC pirates and navies.

Another plus for it, imho, is that Chiara doesn't mind playing it and with 2, it could easily be played in an hour and a half if both players are familiar with the rules. It can end quickly, too, as you can get 50% of the winning points by collecting gold that you secretly stash, so you're never sure when the game will end, which adds a nice bit of tension, if you're using the stash.

What I'd like to explore more is the viability of PvP combat. It seems a bit too easy to dodge combat if you want (which I think is good in a learning environment). This is a detraction I have with the game, but there is also a variant from the designer, Marcus, about fixing that, where you can blockade ports and force a player to at least have a chance to fight you. In vanilla rules, you can sale around with 50-60 gold and it's pretty hard to lose it, unless you really blow it.

Overall, I'd say it's a keeper. Chiara's family really likes the theme and the bits are amazing. They did a top notch job on production. I'd like to try the variants and I imagine will use them solely once people have played more than 2 or 3 times, as they add a bit more of a challenge. (From GCL 1/11/10)

RATING: 9
04/16: Got in a trade against Rampage.
Owned expansion : Seas of Glory

The best pirate game, period. It is pretty long though: I wouldn´t dare to play this with more than 3. A game that feels very thematic and that gives me the freedom I really like to have in board games. 

This game is often compared to Xia : Legends of a Drift System. I must say, I think I like M&M better, even though it lasts longer. The rules are more streamlined, more solid: the game is simply more balanced and playtested than Xia. It feels more elegant, less clunky, less fragile. I still like Xia though, it just can't be taken too seriously as the balance isn't as tight as one would hope and it's pretty luck dependent. Last but not least, M&M plays well with 2 players, where Xia wasn't designed to be played with less than 3 (even though it can work with 2).

Christian Marcussen is probably my favorite game designer at this point. Clash of Cultures is my #1 game of all time and this is in my top 5. 

I haven't played this in a while since I'm painting the minis (and there's a lot of delay).

RATING: 7.5
Excellent tie-in of theme and mechanics.  However, there is a lot more dependence on dice than I was expecting.  For example, to obtain a rumour, there is a mandatory monetary cost + dice roll; if successful, dice are rolled later to see if the rumour is true, and if successful again, dice are rolled once more to succeed at achieving rumour requirements.  Also, there is a tremendous variance in how long a turn takes to execute.  It could be as quick as 10 seconds as you move out of port, from one region to another, and into another port.  Or it could take 10+ minutes as you take ~ 8 port actions, raid a merchant ship, and/or get involved in combat with another ship.  Downtime can seem long even if you play a variant where players take their turns simultaneously when performing port actions.

Played at WifeGonCon 2012.
Purchased from BGGer "Howitzer_120mm", June 2012.

RATING: 8
Se trata de un juego de aventuras en el que somos un capitán de barco en el mar del caribe. A través de las acciones que realicemos nos iremos definiendo como mercante, si nos dedicamos a llevar mercancias de un puerto a otro o pirata si nos dedicamos a asaltar barcos, ya sea de otros jugadores, mercantes o barcos NPC.

En cada turno disponemos de tres puntos de acción que podrás gastar en movernos, actuar en un puerto o buscar/atacar barcos. 

Cuando actuamos en un puerto tenemos a nuestra disposición una buena cantidad de cosas a realizar, comprar y vender mercancías, oir rumores que si los cumplimos nos darán un punto, reparar nuestro barco, mejorarlo o cambiarlo por otro más grande (previo pago claro).

El combate está bastante logrado. Al inicio de cada ronda cada capitán elige una acción entre disparar, abordar o huir. Se hace una tirada que depende de nuestro capitán y el tipo de barco que tenemos, realizándose la acción que eligió el ganador. 

En general el juego es bastante majete y entretiene.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
First, I would rate this game as a 7'5 (because I have doubt a lot if rating it as a 7 or 8 XD). Having said that, I thing that it is a very good game, with some flaws to be taken into account (and this is why I have decided to put a 7), but, overall, it is very fun to play. Let's go for the review:
One of the things that I want in every game that I play is that it is thematic and that the mechanics are well related to the theme. In this case, I think that it works perfectly. You really have the feeling of being a pirate (or a merchant) and being on the Caribbean looking for treasures and gold. I really like the fact that you can play the game in several ways, you do not need necessarily to play as a pirate, a merchant works as fine (in fact, usually better than a pirate, that is one of the issues of the game).
Another positive aspect of the game are the components. Are of a very good quality, very nice and help to feel that you are actually on a ship (a bit of imagination guys). Then, I do think that the ship battles and configuration and improvements are very good. I do like the mechanic and it is fun to improve your ship and fight for the best one, try to capture the huge ships and all of that. But, this has a very negative point, which is what makes the game not that good, and is the fact that, if you lose your ship, specially at mid game, you are out. Ok, they allow you to put another vessel in play and continue playing but, practically, you can leave the table and sit on the sofa.
Positive:
- Highly thematic and mechanics that make total sense
- Wide range of available options (merchant, pirate, try to complete missions, rumors...)
- It is fun to play. Even if you know that you are going to lose
- Very good components and nice design
- Easy to explain and approachable to casual players (maybe not casual, casual)
Negative:
- It is more difficult to have success as a pirate than as a merchant
- The missions and rumors, in reality, are not a good way to go. They provide not enough points taking into account how many turns you need to expend crossing from one corner of the board to the other
- Losing your ship is almost game over. Specially during mid game
- Maybe a good "house rule" is to increase the victory points to 12 or 15, and allowing only to store 50 coins (as it is now). That will reduce the distance between merchants and pirates
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Sounds good so far, length can be tweaked, not sure about the dice though...

Hmmm seems to be quite a few reports of downtime, too long and too random, not exactly good features especially combined...sounds like it misses the mark and will need houserules. 

EDIT - Have now played with 3 players (rating is for 3 too, would definitely be lower for 4) and just about everything I noted above stands. Its a really cool overall package but yet something seemed missing or a little off, could be lack of strategic planning and decision making for a longer game and yes the luck seems too high for the length though it is a pirate game I suppose. Of course most of these things may NOT bother avid AT fans since they are used to them...

Playing a "merchant" can actually come out quite dry for such a thematic game too, your mostly just going to a port, selling, buying and then going to the next port. You have options on upgrading and such but the core of what your doing is somewhat repetitive especially as just a merchant. 

The game should scale well from 2 - 4 though I would not want to play with 4 due to increased downtime, 3 is a good number and 2 would be fine actually. As for the length, simply playing to less points makes a shorter game so really not one of the bigger sticking points for me, no matter the player number 2 hours is really the max for a game like this and that is how I would play it with possibly 90 minutes better yet. For the downtime, with next to nothing to really plan, its the bad kind with nothing to think about. 

I thought that it would be nice to somehow upgrade your "captain" stats (like boats) and this would help mitigate some of the luck (after a battle maybe?) but there was no such option other than firing his ass and paying the penalty to get a new one, some of them are better than others but I think upgrading would have been a good option and getting a weaker one right off the hop is crappy. Options to mitigate some of the dice luck would have been nice too, even card draws could have been pick 3 keep one, etc.  

I own Plunder and would love to play it to compare (which has some doosy warts of its own) and oddly enough this game has captured more than a couple concepts in a game I have close to a Prototype. Hopefully I'll be able to improve on some of the shortcomings but I do wonder now, maybe p/u & del just isn't that hot as a core mechanic...(I still love Die Handler though)

RATING: 8
This game is probably one of the coolest looking ones you'll find. A pretty board, boats, lots of little cards with missions and captains and all sorts of things, treasure chests and money, your own individual game board thing to keep track of your stuff. Pretty much, you look at it and you want to play it. And generally, the game doesn't disappoint. Based on what captain you get and his abilities, you can be a merchant or a marauder. Merchants generally go around collecting goods and selling them. Marauders tend to attack either other players or the non-player characters that are floating around as well. Let's just be honest, this game is pretty complicated. Definitely the most complicated of the ones I've listed here. You basically go from port to port, collecting missions and rumors or doing stuff with the goods, all with the end goal of getting victory points, which can be done in a variety of ways that I'm not going to go into detail explaining, because hell, you can look at the rules for that. It's a pretty fun game that can go really quickly or really slowly depending somewhat on what cards come up and somewhat on what the other players decide to do. But if you like pirates at all, you'll probably enjoy it. It's super thematic.
