RATING: 8
Of any other game I've played, M&M most closely resembles Blackbeard. Blackbeard is a game with huge potential but also some major issues: massive rules overhead and a thematic disconnect in that the main "anti-pirate" forces in the game are card plays from players controlling rival pirates. Merchants and Marauders goes farther toward realizing that potential. There's still a fair bit of rules complexity in the system, but this is mitigated greatly by the fantastic player aids. Whenever a key rule was mentioned during the rules explanation I would search for it on the player aid, and invariably I would find it there. In lieu of take-that cardplay, M&M introduces NPC vessels with straightforward hunt algorithms. This works in a very thematic way; a pirate who has specifically angered the English, for example, will be hunted at top priority by English naval vessels. Spain, however, will only hunt for this pirate if its vessel doesn't have anything better to do at the time, or if Spain happens to be at war with that pirate's home nation.

The aim of the game is for a player to gain Glory, which is acquired in several different ways: defeating another (player or NPC) captain in ship-to-ship combat, completing a Mission, discovering a Rumor to be true, completing a Merchant Raid of at least 12+ gold value, selling 3+ cargo that is "in demand" at a particular port, and upgrading one's ship to a Galleon or Frigate. Also players may stash gold at their home ports (using a ridiculous oversized treasure chest to hide the loot), and count that gold toward their end game glory condition at the rate of 10 gold/1 glory. Only half one's endgame glory may be achieved by stashed loot.

A player can choose whether to become a pirate (by raiding merchant ships and/or attacking non-pirate ships) or remain a law-abiding merchant, buying cargo low and selling it high where it is in demand. Piracy is riskier in that the navies are alerted to one's presence, but also has victory point sources not available to non-pirates. I was able to win my game as a pirate a turn ahead of Justin, who was a merchant. A glance through the game forums reveals other anecdotes of roughly 50/50 balance between merchant and pirate players.

Captains have four major stats which are rated 1-4: Seamanship, an opposed roll on which determines the captain's effectiveness in ship-to-ship combat; Scouting, which determines how easily a captain can find other ships to raid, plunder, and attack; Leadership, which affects crew-to-crew combat and the ability of a captain to recruit replacement crew; and Influence, which represents the captain's social status among the culture of the West Indies and is used for a variety of rolls involving Missions and Rumors. A higher rating means more dice, each of which has a 1/3 probability of a success. Generally one success is required to pass a check.

The game is fantastically detailed; each of the 16 ports has a special ability, there are 20+ different captains who all have different stats and abilities, and the ships all have their own stats and special upgrades available.

It is also an Ameritrash game through and through. There is a lot of dice rolling. None of it feels arbitrary to me; all die rolls can be planned for and the probabilities calculated in advance. But certainly a single session can feel like it was unduly influenced by luck, whether it be lucky dice rolling, a lucky merchant raid card draw, or lucky rumor/mission draws. This is fine for me, because I approach the game as a role-playing experience first, and a strategy game second. There's enough strategy to keep me interested though. The take-that gameplay is relatively toned down, which I find refreshing for a pirate game. Most cards tend to be ones that buff the player who draws them as opposed to screwing an opponent. The only take-that card I saw during our session was a card that allows a player to frame another captain for one of his pirate actions, allocating the bounty to another captain. This may be inconvenient for the framed player but isn't game-breaking at all, and advances the theme.

Update:  less of a game here than I'd hoped.  Perhaps I need to play it with 4.

RATING: 8.5
Ameritrashy pirate game bursting with theme. Beautiful production. Clearly painstakingly researched, I felt I got a bit of a history lesson while playing as pirates. The pirates each have their own "powers," so there's an nice asymmetry that adds to replayability and makes things interesting. RATING: 5
Anyone following the post-release chatter about this game will have noted complaints of imbalance between the game's two overarching paths: trading and piracy. Players are divided about this, which to me speaks to a different sort of mischief afoot in the design. I would say that the imbalance is not between two broad strategies, but between the game's ambitious layers of thematic chrome and the underlying victory conditions. The options available to you seem way, way out of whack with what it takes to win. Several ship types, 8 different ship upgrades, 3 special weapons, a variety of specialists and captains, distinct options in every region of the board... all that, and I buy-low-sell-high for a Glory Point? Or listen/confirm a rumor in much the same fashion?

I want to like this game, but it feels like gamers who simply follow the VP will breeze through the system and miss all the scenery. The narrative arc seems practically non-existent. I also wonder if piracy is simply more interesting than trading. Even if the two are balanced, one should not have the lion's share of complexity.

Merchants and Marauders might be a home run, but I have my doubts. I worry that the designers built a house first and added the foundation later.

UPDATE: After a second play, I give this design a vote of no confidence. I don't think the game buried underneath the chrome is even remotely interesting. The chrome itself seems to float freely, unmoored from any actual purpose. Add to that the fact that, taken as an experience game, there's hardly any narrative arc or sense of accomplishment, and there's not much left to redeem Merchants and Marauders.

RATING: 7
Wow.  Pretty cool game that feels just like "Sid Meier's Pirates!".  The AI of the game is exceptionally well done (how the NPCs adjust their movement to reflect nearby adversaries, how goods are supplied and demanded, how weather is simulated, etc) and the battles are tightly contested.  Some have argued that it's a merchant game with a pirates theme.  I would agree, but alter that statement to say it's a pirate game, with a merchant theme; just like the time it is portraying.  Like any game, you need to weigh the pros and cons of any situation and do what will achieve victory.  Sometimes it will be advantageous to safely ply your trade and avoid conflicts.  Until that is, a rich reward presents itself and you are suitably prepared to seek out battles.  Everything is in here and it feels like and Ameritrash Euro.  Lovely!  I've been eagerly anticipating this game since it's earliest inception as "Age of Piracy" and I've not been disappointed.  The only reason it's a 9 and not a 10 is because it's a long playing game, and so will be difficult to reach repeated plays with my current "Play Group".  However, it's Soll-eed!

RATING: 5
M&M is dubbed as an experience game. But it's not an experience I'm looking out for again. Booooring! Admittedly, all three of us were merchants which isn't the best precondition for an adventurous game. The good thing about this was that it became obvious how simple and luck-dependent the norm strategy for merchants is: buy three of a kind and sail them to a port with demand for that kind. If you don't draw the right cards buy two and sell them in the same port. Repeat until you have three of a kind and sail to the next harbour. Avoid pirates which is not too difficult. In between, players grab and complete/fail rumours and missions as luck will have it. Accumulate one VP for every trade/rumour. Where's the experience in gaining a VP? If M&M wasn't claiming to provide a story, strategic options and playtime wasn't above two hours it would be acceptable. As it is it's just pretentious. M&M got me thinking if the only way to enjoy experience games is (semi-)cooperative (Arkham Horror, Middle-Earth Quest etc.).

RATING: 3
I feel bad rating the game this low, as the production quality is high and I can see that it has been very warmly received.  It simply reflects my willingness to play the game again.  I would refuse except for really extreme circumstances.

In theory I think the dichotomy between merchant and marauder is interesting, but when actually playing the game, being a merchant is really boring (though ended up being a viable strategy), especially since the combat actions are so time consuming.  This leads to an unacceptable amount of downtime that simply is not interesting for the players that are not involved.  I can imagine that once everyone is comfortable with the rules that the experience could pick up speed, but I know that we will not make it there.

RATING: 7.5
2018-02-11 - 7.5 - It really is Sid Meier's Pirates! the boardgame and it is the best pirate game I've played. I really enjoyed it. Our first play took us 3 hours including rules explanation. Even considering some errors we made (which could make the game to go a little bit faster than it should) I think it is a really decent length of play. The theme is there and it is almost everything you could want in that setting. But it is an adventure game and you need to accept that before playing. You can trade, you can arm and fight, or do both. You can have adventures, missions, there is a threat of NPC pirates, of the navy and of the other players too. It can be swingy, you can be lucky (or not), but that's the part of the theme, I think. There is a lot of rolling dice and drawing cards and if you don't like that, it's not the game you are looking for. I'm looking forward to play it again.

RATING: N/A
In Merchants and Marauders, players take on the role of a captain of a small vessel in the Caribbean. The goal is to be the first to achieve 10 "glory" points through performing daring deeds (through the completion of missions or rumors), crushing your enemies (through defeating opponents and NPCs in combat), amassing gold, performing an epic plunder or pulling off the trade of a lifetime, and buying a grand ship. While some points earned from performing various tasks are permanent, players earn points for amassing gold, which can be stolen or lost (or at least diminished) if their captain is killed. Points due to gold are hidden so there's some uncertainty about when the game will end.

RATING: 4
The game seems to have everything to be a blast for me: You choose a captain, get a ship (which can be oriented to commerce or plundering) and sail for glory and fortune during 2 hours or so. The game gives you absolute freedom, so you can switch your approach from commerce to pirating whenever you want -or the other way round, even this can be harder due to the penalties you get to commerce in a territories belonging to a nation you have attacked in the past-. 

There is a lot going on in this game: quests which not only give you immediate benefits but also victory points, ship upgrades and specialists wich improve your maneurability or make you more lethal in battle, naval combat which is simple but gives enough freedom to not feel boring... 

Regarding the drawbacks of the game:

-The captain you get marks your strategy to a certain extend. Indeed, if you get a captain not suited for pirating and you want to follow this approach, you are going to fight an uphill battle. This, I feel, goes against the freedom the game offers you, and for this reason I believe that M&M is one of those games for which asymmetric characters are a con instead than a pro. 

-In a 4 player game, it is not uncommon that at the middle of the game certain players have almost no choice of winning. Moreover, as these players are generally weaker than the leaders, it is almost impossible for them to revert this situation by attacking those in the lead. For a game of the length of M&M, this is a relevant drawback. 

-The game-breaking issue with this game: Pace. The game drags a lot, as it is not uncommon to have to wait 5 to 10 minutes without having anything to do, while your turns can be straightforward. 

All in all, a promising game with a great concept, but with two major drawbacks (pace, rich gets richer syndrome) which make it fall short at the end of the day. Non advisable. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A really cool pirate-themed "euro game" with lots of opportunity for backstabbing, ship-to-ship combat and swashbuckling adventures.  The nice thing is that there are multiple paths to achieve glory (victory) with two main paths being a Merchant or a Pirate (or a little of both). 

VARIANT: We play with 15 Gold per Glory Point when Burying Treasure on your Home Island (max. 5).  Without this variant rule, it is too easy to win using a pure Merchant strategy and also too difficult to win using a pure Pirate strategy.

RATING: 9
As I get older I find I tend to like games with some semblance of theme to them. I have played a million games now where I swap cubes for victory points, and having a different type of auction in them or an elegant turn order mechanic or whatever in them just does not make any difference. And I've impressed so many noblemen and master builders that I shouldn't even have to prove my skill anymore. So, given the chance to do something, I'll usually jump at it. 

Merchants and Marauders is what so many new games forget to be: fun to play. It's one of those games that has a narrative, that you continue to talk about long after it's over. It's got some rough patches, but I will gladly swap fun for cold, burnished "elegance". I even stayed on the straight and narrow the whole game, and won as a merchant, which means, of course, I have to play it again and be a pirate!

RATING: 8
Best pirates game IMO, as of this writing.  It takes a while but I think that is necessary for a game of this many options and for it to feel like a true epic pirate's tale.

You can do pretty much everything that pirates are supposed to do.

It is somewhat of a euro pick-up-and-delivery game.  You have to work that like a machine in order to win the game, and kind of make all the interesting quests/messing with others as side-goals that you only do if it's convenient along your route.  So as long as you understand that it's fine.  But that does feel a little bit non piratey.  At least, it's not a romantic view of piratism.  But it's probably kind of realistic.

There is some luck in some of the expansion components and with where goods come out...but not the kind of luck that bothers me at all.  There are always options available to you, and a lot of the decisions are about how much risk you want to take on.  The risk inherent to attacking other ships or sailing into storms...well it makes sense.  just adds to the theme for me.

Each player not only has a different pirate, but I feel there is an actually unique narrative being spun throughout the game, of where they went to, why they made different decisions, the fighting between other players, the nations going to war...etc.  It always feels like an actual story was told.  One of the best thematic games ever, for me.

Component quality is great.  Obviously the ships are pretty great.  The pirate cardboard tokens for money look really good for cardboard.  I replace them with my own metal money of course.  The map is great.  I guess I hope that they will eventually make another map...let's be the pirate of the indian Ocean, please!  But I could deal with just one map for a long time, especially considerin the Locations component of the expansion.

The expansion adds enough things that I feel the replayability is going to be very high for us.

I like all the stats you have on your captain and ship.  They feel very thematic, and just the right balance of being meaningful in thematic ways, and yet not being so complex that you get really annoyed.

Make no mistake the rulebook is pretty intense for a newbie to boardgames.  You have to set aside the time to learn it well.  But once you do, the experience makes it totally worth it.

I guess my only complaint would be that if it could somehow be all done in a more streamlined way with easier to remember rules...that would be awesome.

Overall, great for both a casual and a lightly competitive experience.

RATING: 5
Great components to an otherwise unenjoyable experience. This game is so punishing to new players AND long duration I can't fathom them coming back a second time. I certainly won't. 

- High variance experience. You can try to plan for your turn, but so many things can happen in between that you often don't get to execute what you originally planned. 
- Low investment to other players' turns, and long downtime between turns. I generally don't care what other players are doing. I care about where they are and where they can reach, but there's no reason to pay ask those questions until it's your turn again. This is particularly true because you're not intended to know your opponents' gold stash / expenditures.
- The hidden gold system combined with paying variable costs is clunky and exacerbated by the 'verification' system. 
- The punishment system of combat (you lose everything and restart minus current VPs) is very punishing. Combine with an obtuse combat system that makes combat prediction difficult, and expect a large ship turnover rate and players feeling like they are just losing turns because they don't understand how to play.

RATING: 6
This just may sum up the game:  long on theme, short on strategic decision-making.  This is after one game, so take my analysis with a grain of salt.  Even so, I suspect I'm right about this.

The captain's stats drive what type of strategy a player should adopt (pirate vs. merchant) - there isn't really a strategic decision to be made as the stats pretty much make the decision for you - and after that the rest of the game is turn after turn of executing on that strategy.  But I'm not sure there are a whole lot of strategic decisions in the execution of a particular strategy.  Players will move from sea space to sea space and do whatever it is their role dictates - merchants buy and sell goods at port and pirates attack other ships.

Put another way, once a player selects a role at the very outset of the game, the player's strategy for the entire game is set.  There don't appear to be any real variations on what a player should do as a pirate, or what a player should do as a merchant.  And if there aren't any variations, are the moves the player makes "decisions," or merely the execution of a pre-determined script?  I have my suspicions about the answer to that, but the theme of the game is enough right now to bring me back for some additional plays.

RATING: 8.6
An exceptionally fun game.  Be ye merchant or pirate, you'll enjoy sailing around the Caribbean, avoiding the ships hunting for you (either naval ships, pirates, or your fellow players WILL be hunting for you), and earning Glory to win the game.

Rules take a little while to get into, but they're quite good.  Combat rules aren't overly complex, though they seem that way at first.

I've always wanted a pirate game like this and didn't even know it.  Kudos to the designers!

[i]*Own Seas of Glory expansion[/i]

RATING: 8
An 'East-India Company' themed game where you can choose to be either merchants or pirates, with various ways to achieve the 10 glory points needed to win the game. The game is very open-ended compared to most board games, and you can do quite a number of things on your turn. However, the game is just a bit too dry when you finish your turn, as you have to sometimes wait 5 - 10 minutes per person to finish their turns. The combat system, on the other hand, works very well and is, in my opinion, the highlight of the game. If you love sea games, you will love this game. For me, I prefer theme-based games, and in this case, 'Merchants & Marauders' is stronger in mechanic than theme.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I thought it would be like Fury of Dracula with Pirates. In some ways it is. That is, it's beautiful, thematic, rather lengthy and rules-complex. They also both have beautiful production and nice bits. Yet it differs in some ways. I think Fury is more confrontational. The only way to beat Dracula is to confront him and kill him. In Merchants, you can win by simply gaining victory points (glory points) whether you choose to be a pirate or merchant. The combat is cleaner in Merchants, so it definitely has a leg up there. Conversely, the combat feels slightly more thematic in Fury, and I appreciate that. Both games are quite random due to heavy card play. If you are looking for a luck-free game, neither would be a good fit. I think I like Fury more, because it's so great to be Dracula. But Merchants might be more balanced because whether you are a pirate or a merchant, you feel like you are building something, not wandering aimlessly around Europe. Geez, they're both soooo good! Definitely pick up Merchants and Marauders though. If you don't mind spending the better part of an afternoon learning the ruleset and writing off the first game as a "learning game," then you won't be disappointed in the long run.

RATING: 7.5
After 1 play:

Fun game, great theme but very long.  I enjoyed the ability to build up (pimp out) one's ship with upgrades to supplement the weaknesses of a particular ship/captain; and also to upgrade to more fearsome ships.

There is also a reasonable amount of downtime on other players' turns and it can be difficult to plan too far ahead - both of which slow the game down.

Reminded me of a computer game generally (in the same way that Eclipse does) but also the specific game of Sid Meyer's Pirates! (which I loved).

Merchant strategy seemed more powerful (odd for a game about pirates), but could just have been the captains we were playing.

While I enjoyed it, I doubt I'd be able to play it much if I bought a copy.  Certainly too long to play with my wife (who likes lighter and shorter games).

RATING: 9
With the endless hours spent on Pirates! in the eighties, there wasn't a minute when I haven't thought back to it playing Merchants & Marauders, and I think it doesn't need more compliment than that. It has everything that Pirates! had ([i]except for stalling for long minutes in the middle of the Caribbean due to dead calm or headwind.[/i])
Very thematic and very dynamic. I loved our very first game, where as a fledgling Dutch pirate I thought that with only one Spanish bounty on my head and with only two Dutch ports in the game it couldn't hurt to attack a Dutch merchant. Three rounds later San Juan was captured by the Dutch, and England was in war with Netherlands. With every Naval ship on my heel, only a few ports available, and two opponents playing a safe game as merchants, I still managed to win, and it [i]felt[/i] like victory.

RATING: 8.5
I really like this game a lot.  Probably one of the best pirate games out there and one of the strongest theme games I have played.  The quality of the components and the art is awesome. One thing that we do is make two event piles, one with ships and the other storms and alternate drawing from each pile.  Even though it means you know that a ship or storm will happen next it makes it more balanced as in some games you could go several rounds with no ships entering play or too many too fast.

RATING: 8.5
This game feels like you're really on an adventure! Imagine you and your ship sailing the Caribbean, trading, doing missions and checking out rumors, raiding ships. Play in a way that you like.

The game involves dice rolls and card draws. This scares off some players. It doesn't scare me off: I enjoy my games, a lot!

As the game's owner, first take your time to read the rules and try out the typical game situations.
The game is on the lengthy side. I'd love to be able to play it more frequently...

I'd love it if I'd be able to play it with 6 players in roughly the same time as a 4-player game now.
I've seen great ideas on the forums and an expansion is coming, someday. I can't wait!

RATING: 9.5
After 1 play with 2 players: 9.5.
This game is long and I can appreciate that there can be downtime with 4 players, but the theme, mechanics and whole experience is tremendous and hits my fav game theme of PIRATES.
The game components are high quality and the rules with examples take a bit of reading but are clear and logically written.
The game play itself is deep and you do have to plan a strategy a few turns ahead to maximise the best cargo/plunder options. The combat with Merchants is fast and against Navies/Pirates/other players becomes clear after the first couple of battles.
After playing with 4 players, I think the downtime between turns becomes noticeable and an issue. With 2 or 3 players the game completes in under 2 hours and is fast. With 4 this is not the case and it really slows the game down. This just means that you need to think carefully how many players you will play the game with before you start.
Yo Ho Yo Ho Me Hearties....... now where's that horizon?

RATING: 8
This is a very thematic game. It really makes you feel like you're exploring the Caribbean Sea and making a fortune through questionable means. Ideally you should play it with people who enjoy the theme of being a captain at sea.

Mechanically, it's quite random and often unfair. Sometimes a player is ruined through no fault of their own. You've gotta know how to take a defeat in good humor to enjoy this, because your beloved captain will certainly be killed.

That said, I believe this is the most authentic pirate game on the market. If you want pirates, then this is the game to get. And make sure you buy the expansion too. It's packed with incredible improvements and I could never go back to the base game after trying it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.9
Un peu trop de temps mort entre les tours, et un facteur chance un peu trop important pour un jeu de cette durée. 

Je n'ai qu'une partie (à quatre joueurs) à mon actif, et possiblement que des joueurs habitués réussissent à jouer plus rapidement...

Il n'y a pas eu aucune attaque entre joueurs, ce qui fait que la seule "intéractivité" avait lieu lorsqu'un adversaire réussissait à modifier la ressource recherchée d'un port...

Un peu déçu aussi de la lenteur de nos déplacements (trois actions par tour) et du mouvement illogique et inconstant des bâteaux pirates ou européens "NPC"; Dans la partie, ces bâteaux européens ont constamment fuit le seul joueur pirate, qui a facilement remporté la partie.

Bref, un très beau design, un thème très présent, une bonne qualité de matériel, mais certaines petites déceptions.

RATING: 7.6
I have a friend [user=angealv][/user] that says this is a REAL thematic game. And he's right. All the rules are completely logical, they make sense and the reflect the reality quite well. You don't get the sense that any of its rules has been designed in order to keep the balance, or make the game more interesting. But the game is balanced and interesting.

It's the best pirate game I have played. The bits are very nice, the art is too... It's a pity there's no Spanish edition :-(
But it drips with theme and it really manages to involve you into sailing through the Caribbean.

It's a combination of pick up and deliver and combat game, with some luck, light tactic and strategy. The luck component is high, it can be a decissive factor: if you get a capitan with low Influence, the others will rack up points with rumours and missions; drawing 3 cards of a kind at the beginning can be a game winner (1 point + lots of money).

It has a big problem: the downtime between turns. Some turns are very short, but when there are Port actions, you can find yourself waiting during more than 5 minutes with nothing to do.

Some other things I didn't like: 
·) Too long: 3-4 hours for a 4 players game.
·) Frigates seem to be underpowered agains Galleons (yes, I know manoeuvrability is very important, but the difference is huge).
·) Luck factor too high, especially with trading (I understand it's necessary to make trading powerful enough to be a competitive activity).

RATING: 8.9
In this game you take the role of a captain/character who starts with a small vessel and  a few crew.  But, the Carribean is your oyster.  From your humble beginnings you can upgrade your ship, or even get a new ship, become a pirate or a peaceful (but well-armed) merchant.  Complete mini-quests, hoard treasure and send your enemies Davy Jones' Locker. 

This game is a wonderful adventure game that offers different strategic paths and a host of tactical issues to consider.  The mechanisms are utterly thematic and the minis and components are very nice.    Each player has their own captain character, with unique stats and abilities.  Some are clearly better as pirates, others as merchants and some could go either way.  It is just plain fun, buying bigger and better ships, upgrading various components, getting special crew members, buying special weapons and completing a variety of mini-quests.  As a pirate, or even as a merchant, you'll be hunted by NPC warships, or even fellow players if they want to risk taking a run at you.  You'll buy and trade cargo at various ports.

You can collect points a variety of ways: hoarding gold, selling volumes of cargo, sinking enemy ships, fulfilling mini-quests and so on.

Most key actions require a bit of luck, but that luck seems manageable.  So the game does rely on risk management skills.  The game is essentially a race to 10 points, so efficiency is also an important skill. Plotting and planning your ship's course carefully will yield points faster and help you avoid getting attacked (unless you want a fight).

The expansion is amazing and adds all kinds of great contents.

There is a solitaire variant here at BGG, which works quite well, because the game already includes rules for non-player ships.

RATING: 7
Wide-open sandbox game with great theme, nice looking bits, very smooth feeling play. Don't own this one but I got to play through several times now. I can see the general shape of the game, but I fear it may drag a bit if folks kind of forget what options they have or get hammered too often or too early. 

Interaction is interesting and feels a lot like a way-toned-down version of the Eve MMO: being a pirate is exciting and high-risk, being a merchant means engaging in careful cat-and-mouse and/or decking yourself out for a strong defensive posture. 

I suspect over more play some issues with randomness may crop up. It didn't feel like I could plan much, but on the other hand each turn I felt like I could work toward roughly planned goals -- go trade this stuff at this place, try for a rumor, try for a mission, watch the pirates and navy ships float around, figure out how to dodge. Curious what diplomacy looks like with four engaged players and a full to-the-end play.

RATING: 7
Lots of thematic richness meaning lots of variety, all spiced by lots of luck. Meaning play for the ride, don't be emotionally invested in the result and don't expect Euro sensitivities. See if you get a card? Roll dice. See if the card you just got pays off? Roll dice. Looking to engage in combat? Roll dice. Combat itself? Roll yet more dice in an awkward convoluted rules sequence that takes a touch of gloss off the game. There's lots of variety in the captains you get and these lead you to try different approaches (pick up and deliver, track down cards, seek combat, etc) so there's enough to explore to earn replay. It's just that it's all a little rules awkward and the game kind of inflicts itself on you rather than the other way around.

RATING: 8
Great Adventures in the Caribbean!! Big Fun in a Med-Heavy Med-Sized Square Box. You get a lot of Game here! You have sailing, pirating, missions, trading, looting, ship building, glory seeking, treasure hunting, bounty rewards, cannons firing, crews fighting, storm dodging, booty stashing, rumor chasing, and more. Each game play becomes a different story. Each captain is unique. Each port is unique. It could be overwhelming at first from all the options, but if you plunge right into this one, your inner pirate will truly emerge, and the game will make a lot of sense. Even AP prone players will move along quickly because of how streamlined the game is, and how strong the theme and game are intertwined.

Still, Be Ye Warned! This is not a gateway game: Lots of particular little rules, initial learning curve, and long gameplay isn't for everyone. But for me, as I learned it, I still had fun, and didn't notice the time going by. There is some downtime, but the rules have that another player acts as the Non-player Ships' Captains in battles, and other players turns can feel like it's part of the story unfolding. 

Great Components. Great Artwork! Need a playing surface larger than a card or coffee table. 

This game reminds me of Runebound a bit in feel.
Thank You for this awesome game, My 2011 Dice Tower Secret Santa.

My rating initially was much higher, but I feel that this game can get too long for what it is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Initally a 'nine', but 5 hour first playtime with 3 players burned everyone out on attempting it again. I have had no real desire to set it up again. Also this is two seperate games: a merchant game, and a pirate game. Doesn't really fit the pirating theme if two players in a 3 player game play merchants and spend every turn doing the same stupid thing: buying and selling and avoiding battles. There is no engagement/battles with other players, which takes all the fun out of it because I play pirate games to have pirate battles against other players not just the NPC's. It's almost solitaire. Rules for battles are hard to explain for newbies and rule book needs constant referencing.

For a high luck game, it's too complex and takes too long to play. Yes, play time could go down on subsequent plays, but first impressions make the most impression so I will have a hard time convincing my wife and limited playing partners to try this again and these are people who actually enjoy playing 'Blackbeard' from Avalon hill. Components are great, but there's a lot of set up time and table space is a priority. 

'Pirate's Cove' (a $4 salvation army find) turned out to be a much better fit for us. It's just as random, but plays much faster (2 hours on first play), components are just as good or better, rules were learned in very short time, and most importantly, has more player interaction. Pirate ship battles between players AND Npc's can happen all the time, and are not things to be avoided. You are still buying and selling your treasures (being a merchant) but you are also FIGHTING like a real pirate should. There's much less fear of battle, and even a reward system for those who retreat. My wife is happy to go into battle now. I love it.

How 'pirates' cove' can be ranked 516 while 'merchants and maruaders' is at 85 is beyond me. I think it's the cult of the 'new' that is keeping this game ranked so highly.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
This is a long-ish pick-up-and-deliver game with a combat element.  Players try to get to 10 points by either trading or being aggressive.  The problem is, trading is very low-risk and nets both money and points, where combat (whether with other players or NPCs) tends to yield less money and is incredibly risky--sooner or later, someone is going to lose everything they've earned (except for their points).  So really, the best way to deal with combat is to avoid it, which makes a lot of the "moving parts" of the game seem superfluous.  I can see games where everyone tries to militarily gang up on anyone who goes for a pure merchant strategy, but that sort of emergent behavior certainly won't come out in your first few plays.  On the whole, there are better pick-up-and-deliver games out there, and if you're looking for piratey themes with similar combat mechanics, try Pirate's Cove.

(1 play)

RATING: 8.5
Pirate simulation game, which really resembles the [thing=73447]Sid Meier's Pirates[/thing] video game. It's an action-point allowance game, where players can follow either the merchant or the pirate route, or both, to earn Glory Points. It's very interesting, but extremely heavy and long. Be prepared for a marathon game during your first play; I'd suggest playing a 6-point game to keep it shorter. I would definitely give it another chance, but it's not something I'd play every day.

RATING: 8
The tabletop equivalent of Sid Meier's Pirates!
Seas of Glory expansion highly recommended

Plenty of bits to play with.

Players can trade, fight, smuggle, explore, investigate rumours, hunt the  Spanish Treasure Fleet, recruit crew, personalize their ship, buy different ships and loads more.

The only real issue is player interaction or the potential lack of. Unless all players turn pirate it's really unlikely that anyone will be involving themselves in anyone else's game - however, this is slightly negated if one player starts storming up the glory track - in which  case they may find themselves the very centre of attention.

A fun game, some periods of heavy downtime but a few rum and cokes and eye patches and all will come away with some tales to tell down the taverns.

RATING: 7
One 3-player game only so far.

Fun game with severe down-time (or was it maybe just us not beeing used to the rules the first time playing?)

There is a lot of freedom in choosing your path to glory. And you can actually do a lot of different things to gain points. You can even start as a Merchant and then - if you feel like it - plunder a ship and start taking your chances as a pirate.

Like:
Buying add ons to your ship
The battles between ships
Beautiful lush artwork (well, except for the box cover)
Tension of sailing with lots of gold (should you risk another shipment/plunder nearby or should you cash in in your home port?)
The coffin - what have the others collected: are they going to trigger the end of the game, do I still have a chance of pulling this or that?
Freedom (you are not boxed in in a thight mechanic framework, one of the main things with M&M is not to try to decheffier the system for optimized moves)
As a player you are a certain person (a captain) with certain skills: You can improve somethings by improving your ship, but you still get advantages and disandvantages from the character and you'll have to adopt your play after that (especially when choosing your carrer)

Dislike:
Down time (?)
Its not complex, but there are lots of rules
"Freedom" - the "loose" mechanical framework does not in it self present any challanges. Or rather, it actually does, but it's another kind of challange cause you'll have to play imagniative/more active. (It's a positive thing about the game as well - se above).
Many things boils down to "just" throwing dices (battles, rumours, missions etc) or set collection (GP when shipping, Merchant raids).
The end game can be somewhat of an anticlimax, still the game in it self feels "too long for what it is".


=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Such a fun game. The theme is outstanding. We had a blast playing it and the time just flew by.

Pros: 
-Incredible theme
-So many choices and decisions you can make throughout the game
-The luck feature in the game is accurate and to the theme, despite what other gamers say. A huge part of being a captain was dealing with luck. I wouldn't have it any other way.
-High replay-ability due to the sheer number of things that can be done in the game. No two games will be alike
-The board and miniatures are beautiful
-Even better when pirate music is playing in the background and you've got some Caribbean drinks 

Cons:
-The naval combat is very confusing. We're still trying to master it
-It's a long run-time, especially for new players. Be prepared for this to be the only game you play on your game night unless everyone knows exactly what they're doing each turn. Even then, you're looking at at least a two hour run time. But it's so worth it, so this really isn't much of a con
-I wish the game would allow for more players. 5-6 would be great, and just lower the glory point goal amount to keep the run-time the same
-There are so many moving parts and things to remember. This keeps things exciting and fresh, but you'll find yourself forgetting that you had this ability or that card you could have played, but were too busy doing 8 other things to remember it.

Conclusion:
Despite the cons (which really aren't that big a deal), this game is a masterpiece. I recommend everyone pick this up and try it at least once. It's going to take some time to learn and explain, but once you master it, it will probably be one of your favorite games in your collection.

RATING: 9.5
The definitive pirate themed game. Unlike the rest of the fantasy based pirate board games this is as close to the real thing as you are going to get. I highly recommend the modular expansion "[url=https://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/161167/merchants-marauders-seas-glory]Seas of Glory[/url]" which greatly improves the base game in so many ways. Complaints about randomness and luck are mitigated with the favors expansion. While complaints about stashing gold are solved with the "Give Me Glory or Give Me Death" variant.

Pros:
* Extremely high production value.
* Quality components with a beautiful game board.
* Multiple paths to victory.
* Sandbox environment - do you want to be a merchant, pirate or a mix of both?

Cons:
* [b]-.5 for the inclusion of female pirate captains which is unrealistic in a non-fantasy game - removed from game.[/b]
* Player boards should include holes to prevent cubes from moving.
* Player boards should include a separate location for your gold.
* Player boards should include a separate location for your glory cards. (Added in the Seas of Glory expansion)
* Pirate characters should be chosen by limited selection not distributed randomly. (Variant added in the Seas of Glory expansion)
* Small cards are hard to shuffle.
* Minimum 3 hour game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.56
Awesome pirate-themed adventure game similar in feel to something like Runebound (though a little shorter & lighter on rules).

The cards work well to keep things unpredictable, the different ship/captain abilities permit different styles of play, and the way the dice & counters work during naval combat matches the theme very well (maneuvering for position, cannon firing, and use of grapeshot & chainshot).

Appears to be plenty of replay value given the number and variety of cards, and the various different approaches you can take.

Component quality is ok, but all the cardboard components appear to have some kind of thin waxy/plastic coating that can tear and/or peel if not careful. It looks like the same stuff used in "Duel in the Dark". Unfortunately, the factory-packed box allowed the ships to poke into the game board leaving dents!

Rules are reasonably written, but there are a lot of important pieces of information in the wrong place, with not even a reference to them. It reminds me of the style of FFG rules - nicely-written, but in conceptual order rather than in play-sequence. While learning, this leaves you flicking between multiple pages just to ensure you haven't missed anything when performaing a simple action. One simple example (there are many more), why isn't the "flip the face-down ship mod token" rule included as the first port action in the bulleted list? Instead, it is buried under the "buy ship mod" section.

Similarly, the summary cards are decent, but have a few vital pieces of information missing. Would not recommend playing a first game by relying on them to remind you of all the major rules & sequences of actions.

Still, the game plays great once you've got the rules sorted!


WARNING: Biggest problem experienced is with 2 players, a predominantly-merchant player seems to easily outscore a predominantly-pirate player at a rate of at least 2:1, especially if they start at opposite ends of the board (making for the pirate to interfere before the merchant gets established). Really need to ensure we're playing correctly, study pirate strategy and maybe look for variants.

Some suggestions to aid pirate players include...
- NPCs move 2 sea zones & can hunt instead of each of those moves
- limit number of points allowed from each source (battles, stash, rumours, missions, etc.)
- reduce cost & sale price of frigate (or increase those of galleon)
- reduce number of cargo cards drawn by 1 (eg. from usual 6 cards down to 5 cards)


FAQ & ERRATA (In Progress): http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/595002/faq-wip-you-can-help/page/1

SLEEVES: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/article/6000927

RATING: 9
I respect this game because it perfectly fulfills its purpose. This game makes you feel like you're a pirate. It doesn't have the deepest strategy or the clearest rules or the quickest pace, but it does well enough in each of those categories, and none of that matters if you think the idea of being a pirate who goes around around searching for treasure and smashing enemy ships and looting everything is awesome. You get to do all sorts of cool pirate things that other games either don't include or implement via awkward and/or broken mechanics, and you won't find anything awkward or broken in this game. The production value is also through the roof, which is nice to see. In the end, this game will sink or swim based on how much you like the theme; if you think you'd like this game, you will, and if you think you won't, you won't.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a great game.  It is real gamey and not a simulation of pirates.  The characters have no names that I recognize, too bad, that would have made it more fun.  But it captures the fun or sailing around as a merchant and then deciding when to become a pirate, if ever. Great theme.

You pick up cargo, deliver cargo, fight off naval ships and pirates, which have a mind of their own.  Pirates hunt any non pirate and naval ships hunt pirates.  Real nice.

The game is colorful, components attractive, and rule book is pretty good.  Didn't have to come to boardgamegeek to understand the rules, which means the rules are pretty light and easy to figure out.

All in all an addictive game that captures the fun, not the simulation, of being in the Caribbean during the golden age of pirates.  

Just finished playing solo with 4 characters.  2 of the characters I played as pirates and 2 as merchants.  

Here are some problems.  I would definitely get the expansion, Seas of Glory as it cleans up some of the balance and adds a lot more things to do.  In fact, that is one of the problems.  There is way to much to do.  Lots of ways to win, but if you go for the win quickly, you will miss so much of the game.  I wanted to slow it down a lot so I could enjoy all the things I could do and even then I couldn't do as much as I wanted. I really enjoyed exploring the game and then when I got everybody up to a good level and had seen a lot, I went for the win, and it went pretty quick after that.  A great advantage to playing it solo.

When you become a pirate, you limit your choices to make money and such.  Playing a pirate is a lot harder but you do get to attack a lot more.  That takes time and may not get you any victory points, whereas the merchants can just roll along.  Some of the pirates bots are pretty weak too, making it easier for the merchants.  One of my pirates went back to being a merchant because they were not getting much done.  I would strengthen up the pirate players and somehow strengthen up the pirate bots.

So I made up some house rules to make the game more fun for me.  See the files section for those rules.

All in all, a strong 8, but with my rules a stronger 9.  Nothing is perfect but this game is a lot of fun to play.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Christmas 2010 gift.  

I love playing this title for so many reasons.  There are enough cards, ships and captains to try so many different things.  You can play from beginning to end with only one captain and win, you can cycle through a few different captains and ship types and also win while using contrasting merchant or pirate styles.  

You can battle NPC military ships (which are usually very hard and briefly manned by another player), you can raid NPC merchants which are usually much easier targets for acts of piracy.  Then there is Hunting Player pirates or playing the pirate and raiding other players.  The options within a game, just never seem to cease!

Alternatively you can be an honest merchant or a ship for hire performing a myriad of missions.  You can be adventurous and prove or disprove rumors picked up ship ports.

You can play quite quickly 2 1/2 to three hours or longer games running four to six hours by simply not capping the Glory track to ten; its quite flexible.

We prefer to play with the cut throat beta proposed by Christian.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.25
Merchants & Marauders is an experience.  It is one of the first boardgames I have ever played that makes it feel as if there is a little world playing out before you as player and NPC ships sail about the board attempting to further their goals.  Honestly, between the event cards and watching the ships, I felt a level of immersion I use only feel in RPGs or videogames.

Now, the question is, do you like immersion in theme? If you do, and you like pirates, you should get this game immediately. 

There are a lot of die rolls that can screw you over - and the mission cards are unbalanced - and the glory cards vary widely in power level.  But you know what? I don't care, because it all *works* together to make it seem like you are a pirate (or merchant) on the high seas.

I likely wont get to play this one *quite* as much as I would like because it does take several hours to play (at least 2 and a half to 3 and a half for a 4 player game), but I understand that in a game with as much stuff going on as this one has, it has to take a while.

Positives: 
    -Wonderful immersive pirate theme
    -Ship combat is a lot of fun
    -Very nice components (especially the ship miniatures and the treasure chests)
    -Has lots of depth and replay value in my opinion
    -Is easily modded to your tastes if you so choose
    -Is well supported by its creator, Mr. Marcussen, who seems to be a really nice guy :)

Negatives:
    - If you are opposed to dice rolls you won't like it, but if you *are* opposed to dice rolls, why did you play it anyway? :)
    - Longish playing time (but worth the time investment!)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
*UPDATE - I'm bumping my score up to 7. Even though it's fiddly, chaotic and slow, it's still more fun and more epic than the other games I've rated 6 on BGG.*

If you want a highly thematic piracy game that's fiddly and random, this is it.

The randomness doesn't only influence your success. It also constantly changes your individual objectives, which unfortunately creates a feeling of 'the game playing you'.  On the plus-side, it means frequent, sometimes fun, tricky decisions.

It has excessive bookkeeping. Players are constantly checking that they haven't forgotten to activate a range of things described on random cards. They also have their own hand of text-filled cards and other tokens that they must try to remember to activate at the right time. It's almost inevitable that you'll forget things. The expansions add even more things into the game that need to be managed.

The downtime between turns is high, which is why I prefer to play this as a two-player game.

Unlucky players can find themselves in almost irrecoverable positions very early in the game, especially if a luckier player acquires a massively upgraded ship and decides to blast them back to the start of the game (the map also spawns non-player enemy ships that can do the same). It annoys me that one of the expansions add a Loyalty track which can let you travel further around the map in order to attack another player, which basically means unlucky players become constantly threatened and limited in what they can do.

The above problems are a shame because the individual elements are great. It has all the variety and events you could want in a pirate game and you DO feel invested in your ship. Importantly, the combat is also fun.

If you have the patience of a buddhist monk you probably won't notice it dragging and will think it's the ultimate pirate game.

Personally, I'm getting a bit bored with these giant sandboxy games that have tons of fiddly and slightly 'meh' decisions i.e. the many dull Cthulhu/Lovecraft games. Yet I keep coming back to Merchants & Marauders because it has enough fun elements and such magnificent theme.

RATING: 8
Sleeves: arcane tinmen small/red

A delightful game that is unfortunately a bit too rules heavy for many people to really enjoy that crucial first game. It's not complex per se, there is just so many things you can do. Two - three really - different modes of battle. Like 7-8 different actions you can perform in a port. And on top of that every space on the board has it's own special rule (printed on the board, thankfully). I love it - I really do - but I can see how it might feel a little overwhelming at first..

There is also tons of luck involved with the dice. I've gone from "okay, just sail back to my home port and it's a wrap" to being sunk on the way, and then having 5 other captains die on me in my mad scramble to get back in the race, before losing by a mile. So if that sounds terrible, you probably won't like it!

RATING: 5
Dripping with piratey theme goodness, but I was not super excited about it after the first game, especially for a 3+ hour game, and I definitely would prefer to play Merchant of Venus, which has just as much theme but is a purer pick-up and deliver game. I would be interested in trying this again with just 2 players; anymore than that and I'll pass.  I particularly don't like the 3 actions per turn mechanics, which makes movement around the board very deterministic (I also complain about getting screwed by the dice in Merchant of Venus, but there are upgrades to mitigate this if you want to invest, whereas there's no way in M&M to move faster).  I think I would have liked it better if there was more of a historical component, with real history about how different countries went to war and hunted down privateers, eliminate any player vs. player attacking (this was never a popular mechanic in the original MoV), and simplify the combat mechanics.

Update: After 2 solo games and a 2p game, I am lowering the rating.  I do not want to play it again.  Battle is so tedious when it does occur (which we avoided as much as possible) - Pirate's Cove and Winds of Plunder do battle and ship arms race dynamics much better. And what M&M is pretty good at - pick-up and deliver - is done much better by Merchant of Venus.

RATING: 8
I agree with the general sentiment that pirates in this game seem to have a significantly tougher go of it than merchants. I will admit, however, that this is likely due to my inexperience and my small number of plays through the game. Despite this very small wrinkle in my merchants and marauders experience, I find the game highly enjoyable. The combat mechanisms balance chaos with true risk-management and clever tactics, and I really appreciate the "NPC" ships - they strongly emphasize the consequences of your choices. The port actions are wonderful in their strong thematic grounding (I am speaking primarily of the "rumor" option - what a fun action to visualize and carry out!), and everything comes together to make for a rich pirate experience.

RATING: 5
Very flavorful, and at heart it wants to be a simulation of everything that involves pirates. Too bad that the game, in itself, suffer greatly of the runaway leader problem. Once the luck of the first plays has made some player even slightly more powerful than the others, there are nigh to 0 reason to not hunt for those weaker ships and send them to the bottom. While recover from an early death is possible, and it's fun and flavorful in the process, to catch up with the winning players is simply not feasible. Maybe a simpler, shorter, but more balanced game would have been better for those who like flavorful game but can't simply let go of their competitive side.

RATING: 8
I don't really like adventure games, but I love M&M. I guess it's partly the theme and how well mechanics reflect it, and partly that it's just great fun to play. The great thing about is (apart from excellent production) is the plurality of career choices. There's no clear cut between being a pirate and a merchant, but instead you get bounties for every act of piracy from the nation against which you transgressed. A pirate's life might be tempting, but when naval ships start to track you and you are banned from visiting a port for repairs, you might regret it. Even more so, that some of the missions you can claim or rumours you can investigate will be unavailable for you.

My review: http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/719416/insight-into-merchants-marauders-an-adventure-ga

RATING: 9
Contrary to what a geekbuddy of mine said, this IS the Sid Meier's Pirates! game that you were looking for! With this game you experience a story, you have a narrative and it is nail-biting exciting to go against a man-o-war and win, barely alive. The multitude of options available to to gain points and explore the story are truly awesome. I want to play this game all the time.
 
Nonetheless there are some minor things I don't like, probably because I haven't figured them out yet. 
* Other players playing a merchant are annoying and lame. It's the accountant tactic of winning this game and I wonder, if we should make it mandatory for every player to have at least one bounty from any one nation.
* The rumours and the missions are cool, and I would like to do them more often, but it seems very rarely that you get the chance to do one of them. 
* The Specialists are cool, but I need to pay more attention to them. 
* There need to be more things happening. The first time we played wrong and we had an event card whenever a player took his turn. There were a lot of frigates and pirates in the water and we saw a lot more action. Last time we almost only drew storms, which are a bit boring, because they only limit your turns. 

So, my heart says '10', my gut says '7', so I go with a [b]'9'[/b] in the end.

RATING: 6
Full of fun and flavour, but with a few gaps in the rules that need to be filled with logic. Very dependent upon who you're playing with. It tends to fall flat with players who don't want to act a little pirate(y) and instead play like polite peace loving dullards. A little aggression and biffo makes it a lot more fun. So I found it fun to play with children - they get the idea - if you see an opportunity to pinch stuff you should usually go for it. With the right crowd this rates at least a point higher.

I find the game nicely balanced between merchant actions and piracy. You pick your battles, where you want to fight them and against who you want to fight. The game has a clever bounty system where you deal with the consequences of aggressive actions for a quick buck or to stop another player just from making off with a pile of spoils. It's clever, it's interactive and with players who know the rules the port visits and combat run along at a nice pace. That said I prefer to play with three players to keep the game moving quickly and coming in at under two hours. (What's all this about port actions taking too long? Sell, buy, maybe rumour roll, maybe fix ship. The whole shebang takes about 30 seconds.)

There's luck in the cards and dice rolls, but all that is acceptable because there's plenty of cards and plenty of dice rolls. It's about the fun and it delivers.

RATING: 7.5
I don't want to damn with faint praise but the best I can say about this one is - not bad. It looks good - the rules seem fairly easy to grasp and apply - BUT. The game is quite fiddly - there can be an awful lot of downtime between turns, and I'm not completely happy about this stashing rule, which enables a player currently on 4 points to suddenly win immediately due to winning 1 more point and adding his stash. (Even though that's how I won the only game I played.) 

I don't want to say I dislike the game - I might play it again but won't be looking hard for the opportunity to do so. It's certainly a game of an appropriate quality such that I would recommend trying it out at least once - the theme works well and I can see that many gaming groups might make this a favorite, but it's not exactly my cup of tea, and too much downtime would be my main criticism.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This is the board game that's given me the closest thing to a feeling of roleplay, in spite of never getting into Sid Meier's Pirates (though it satisfies the Grand Theft Auto itch! And definitely Assassin's Creed Black Flag now that I've played the video game) or even roleplay itself. Mechanisms are simple, just action points, but everything is dressed up in a rich way that made me care. I was totally bummed when my pirate died.

The killer app in the game is the merchant/pirate duality and the sandbox/freedom to make your own choices. 'Morality' is all the rage in video games nowadays, and this one gives heavy consequences for choosing a life forever on the run. Be an inefficient merchant, stuck at least every other turn adrift at sea, or be a pirate, getting to conduct both a port action and steal cargo from merchant ships, but be able to survive the target on your back and the hostility of ports that no longer welcome you. It's easy to switch from a merchant to a marauder, but when should you do it, if at all?

This feels like a 9 right now, but should settle between 8-10. 5 things hold me back:

1) Will other games play out in the same 2-3 general themes (barring some random luckiness): be a pirate and hope the naval ships take a while to mobilize; or wait for a Galleon before being violent. The sheer number of cards in the game and possible combinations gives me optimism. Old-school Z-Man hasn't balked at cramming the box with tons of cards which you only use a few of in games like this and Earth Reborn to add variety and unpredictability. This, along with Mage Knight, puts Fantasy Flight's usual 10-20 play crop of cards to shame.

2) [-]The Event deck was pretty boring.[/-]

3) Glory cards reinforce runaway-leader syndrome. Maybe these balance the fact that early leaders get targeted, but I'm not sure you can target players effectively this game, especially if their early lead gets them a ship upgrade quickly.

4) Game could drag with the wrong group. You can spend many consecutive turns grinding and not doing anything meaningful, and that would be a frustrating time if other players bog down in AP.

5) Biggest gripe: player vs. player conflict appears to be dominoes/pile-on. Nobody dares to initiate, then when it happens, whoever wins is so wounded that the other players swoop in for the kill. Maybe lower rewards (don't give the Glory Cards to the victor for a successful boarding too!), decrease the penalty of starting over, or tweak battles so that the luckily targeted loss of any non-Cargo stat doesn't cripple your ship.

6) With 4) and 5) taken together, there isn't much direct interaction, with gameplay often being do your own stuff, then watch others with interest. If watching others gets old, it'd make the non-me time (2/3 or 3/4, or longer if others have AP) a killer.

Based on what I've heard of the expansion, I feel confident it'll address some of the base-game issues (e.g. Galleons) and push this to a 10.

3er was fine, but 4er felt better (in spite of more downtime) because the board got more crowded and incubated conflict in a more natural manner than the PvP scouting rule variant. Maybe that variant is still necessary for 3er.

5+5

[color=gray][b]Favorite 4-player Long - Runner-up[/b][/color]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
So, I finally got to play the physical embodiment of what I always thought Sid Meier's Pirates could be.  It's a good game that makes me think of Arkham Horror on the high seas.  Many gamers might give this an 8 at best, but the theme appeals to me strongly.  A couple of major drawbacks are the teaching time for people that are not familiar with the PC game as there are a lot of elements to explain as well as the play time as not everyone wants to play a 3-hour game.  I think that this game improves with more players as well as the cutthroat variant mentioned by the designer as it prevents the merchant characters from scurrying from port to port without threat of harm.  All in all a good game, but not one of my top 10 - at least for now.

Playing it again at Lobster Trap, I have seen how important it is to play it more frequently so you remember the flow of play.  It can bog down if folks aren't familiar with what can be done.  Still a solid, fun game dripping with theme and I hope that playing it recently will get it to the table more frequently.

RATING: 8
Very cool game about trade and piracy in the Caribbean. It feels like the heavy Euro daddy to DoW's light game Pirate's Cove. It's action driven, so in theory the game plays fairly quickly, but I think the first game is definitely a slow learner's game. You need to get a feel for how trading works to make money, how ship combat works, pros and cons of piracy vs trading and how the different captain skills affect the different parts of the game, etc.

We really enjoyed the the "open world" feel of the game. Despite playing on a map with only 17 spaces, the presence of naval ships from the four colonial powers, the effects of war on where you can port, deciding when to go pirate and upon which nation to prey, etc. all felt "big" to me. Some players sailed long distances to make desirable sales, some ran away from hostile ships. I spent the last part of the game jumping from port to port trying to avoid the powerful pirates around me.

I'm really looking forward to playing again now that we've seen the game in action once.

This is another one I may regret trading away, but I didn't see it coming to the table at home.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
[2012-05-05]
Nagyon nagy népszerűségnek örvendő játékot nagy várakozással próbáltam ki, csalódni nem csalódtam, de nem is éreztem elsöprő érzést. A játékosok kereskedőként indulnak a játékban, de később, ahogy drága árukat szállító hajókat látnak meg kalózokká válhatnak. Valószínűleg csak kereskedőként nehéz a játékban a nyerés, de talán nem lehetetlen. Több fajta hajónk lehet a játékban, de talán túl egyértelmű melyik a legjobb hajó így maximum egy váltáson esünk át a játék során, hacsak háború nem tör ki. A hajócsaták mechanizmusa jól megoldott. Nagyban függ a szerencsétől, hisz kockadobások sorozata, de azért a jobb kapitány, jobb hajó nagy előny. És itt az egyik buktató, a jó kapitány. Ezt a játék elején sorolással kapjuk és közben nem lehet változtatni. Egy-egy kapitány jól behatárolja, hogy a játékosnak mire kell mennie, különben nem sok esélye van. A játék kivitele szép, sokat dobnak a műanyag hajók is rajta. A játék fő erénye számomra a téma szinte tökéletes megvalósítása. Játék közben érezni, hogy valaki kalózként, hogy próbál menekülni az esetleges erősebb nemzetek hajói elől, próbál kereskedőket elkapni és csencselni. Érdekes és változatos az egyes kikötők előnyei, amelyek a hajózásra késztetik a játékost. Jól kigondolt a játék, jól adja vissza a kalózkodás érzését. A baj nálam három dologban jelentkezik. Először is a magas nyelvfüggőség. Minden kártyán szöveg, nem is kevés, hosszú összefoglalók, városok, különböző fejlesztések szövegei. Nagyon sok szöveg. Ezek persze mind a beleélést hivatottak segíteni, de azok számára, akik nem perfektek angolból inkább negatívan hatnak. A másik dolog a szerencsefüggőség magas volta. Érdekes módon annyira nem vettem észre a játékom során, mert nagyon jókat dobtam végig. De belegondolva sok minden múlt a jó dobásokon. Zavaró a kapitány véglegessége. És a játék legnagyobb baját hagytam a végére, az iszonyatos holtidőt. Egy játékos akár mozoghat, csatázhat és kikötőbeni tevékenységet is folytathat a körében, ami nagyon elnyúlhat. Négy játékos esetén 1 óra szabálymagyarázat után több, mint 4 óra volt a játék és én még pörgettem is. Akár jóval tovább is elhúzódhatott volna. Jó játék a M&M, érhető is a népszerűsége, mert jó adja vissza témát, de nálam a hosszú holtidő rontott az összképen, de kap majd még esélyt.

[2012-05-19]
Megkapta az esélyt, egyet rontok a ponton. Nagyon jó téma, jó megvalósítás, de a három kellemetlen dolog megvan. Nagyon magas holtidő, négy játékosnál nagyon hosszú játékmenet, pedig próbálja a játék rövidíteni magát azzal, hogy a győzelemhez szükséges pontok felét aranyból be lehet szerezni és nem is nehéz 50 aranyat összeszedni a játékban. Nagy nyelvfüggőség és legnagyobb bajom talán a nagy szerencsefaktor. A jó arány nincs eltalálva ez esetben. Tehát, hogy túl komoly és hosszú a játék ilyen magas szerencse mellé. Némi apróság még, hogy igazából 5 fajta hajó van, abból egy csak különleges eseménykor szerezhető az alapból választható kettő után pedig a fejlesztéskor vehető kettő közül teljesen egyértelműen az egyik erősebb, mint a másik így nincs választás. Tehát ebben nincs igazán változatosság. Nagyon könnyű elsüllyeszteni valakit, akinek így kb. véget is ér a játéka, tehát effektíve nem lehet kiesni, de gyakorlatilag onnantól vegetál csak a megsemmisített játékos.

RATING: 9
Best with 4 players.

Absolutely in love with the theme. What a neat game. I should play it more but it seems to be far and away best with 4 players which easily increases the length to 3 hours or more, and there is very stiff competition in the 3+ hour game category. It also feels pretty satisfying -- like something you always have fun with, but you don't feel the need to play too often.

One thing I've found is that every player needs to be in to the theme for full enjoyment, otherwise downtime during the port "action" and the battles can seem like a lot. Personally I don't mind, because I'm so into the pirate theme that I'm as genuinely interested in the fate of the other players as I am my own!

This game has beautiful, fun components, and a generous amount of cards for an unexpanded game. Still, I'd love to see more variety (and NPC movement) in the event deck, as it could be the source of a lot more fun and excitement if it were more varied.

Pretty much a perfect game IMO. I have almost no rules-related complaints. Almost as thematic as Battlestar Galactica, and almost as fun as Cosmic Encounter.

[b]2 player:[/b] Not enough conflict. Plays relatively quickly though and is a pretty fun race, and if committed combat does occur... well, it will probably decide the game!
[b]3 player:[/b] Awesome. Faster than 4 player, but not as good
[b]4 player:[/b] Perfect player count!

(5 Design + 4 Enjoyment)

RATING: 8
This is a deep but extremely enjoyable pick up and deliver game.  I think what I love most about it is your ability to adjust how you play it each time depending on circumstances.

At the start of the game you are dealt a captain card.  Much like the name of the game suggests your two main courses of action are to either play the game as a pirate, marauding merchants and naval ships with a bounty on your head.  Or as a law-abiding merchant carrying goods from port to port and battling pirates for the bounty they offer.

The choice you make is very dependent on the captain you are dealt.  They each have a set of stats and a special ability.  This should tell you how to play the game to best effect.  It's not even usually about just pirate or merchant either.  In fact, most of the time the choices are a lot more granular.  For example, in my first game of this my captain had great stats for finding and marauding merchant ships but not so great in outright battle with naval ships.  Another player had a special ability that let him choose from more cargo cards at specific ports but wasn't so great at discovering rumors to acquire.

The amount of decisions to be made as well as the open-world nature of game play and variety of cards and outcomes make this an amazing game.  I was very, very pleased with it.  If it were only a little bit shorter it would be one I'd want to play all the time.  But at 3+ hours it simply isn't one you can bring out too terribly often and is complicated enough that it's certainly not for everybody.

RATING: 6.7
[i]Gameplay depth[/i] [b]4[/b]
[i]Immersiveness[/i] [b]9[/b]
[i]Elegance[/i] [b]6[/b]
[i]Aesthetics[/i] [b]9[/b]

This game is a very double-edged sword. One on hand there are the aesthetics and the theme. Apart from the cards (they are too small, especially the captain cards, and are underwhelming as a result), this game looks and feels amazing, especially the ship miniatures, and really makes you feel as if you are roaming the seas as a pirate or a merchant, which is very impressive. On the other hand, there is the aggravatingly slow and luck-based gameplay. You don't get to do a whole lot in one turn, which is especially annoying because it can take a while before your next turn arrives. For the few choices you can make, dice rolls determine the outcome of these choices way too much. All in all, because I buy a game not just to look at but to actually play, I was very disappointed with Merchants & Marauders.

RATING: 7.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is the best pirate game I've played. Each player takes the role of one of 16 captains, each of whom has strengths and weaknesses which should be taken into account when deciding whether the best course is to lead the life of an honest merchant, or raise the jolly roger and go pirating.

The theme is extremely well realized. There are five different ship types, and various modifications and special weapons which can be added to enhance them (at a price). Or you may even take one as a prize. Combat resolution is fairly complex and involved, so when two ships battle it will require some time to resolve, even for experienced players. The rest of the game moves quickly, though. There is a much abbreviated resolution for pirates attacking non-player merchant ships. Merchant players will spend more time buying and selling trade goods, and tend to avoid combat more often than not.

There are non-player naval ships, pirates and merchants which must be taken into account, as well as missions, rumours and events, so those who yearn to immerse themselves in the world of Hollywood pirates are in for a treat. (If your tastes run to clean, luck free eurogames, you should run away screaming.)

It's a rich brew when taken all together, filled with interesting tactical choices. My only criticism is that the rules are a bit scattered, but the designer does a fine job of providing answers and support to ease the learning curve. If your tastes are like mine, you owe it to yourself to check this game out.

RATING: 9
Hooray!!!  I FINALLY have the pirate game I've been waiting for all these years - an open-ended, swashbuckling adventure with different routes to victory!  And interestingly enough, you don't even need to ever become a pirate, remaining a wealthy merchant who is braving the dangerous seas (but what fun would that be?).  The game design is excellent and players get into the flow of the game quite quickly.  It can feel like there are a lot of fiddly rules, but that's the trade-off for having a lot of options in the game.  In fact, the openness of the design lends itself wonderfully to house rules, and I've even added a couple of new elements in the form of [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/608859/initial-ideas-for-squashs-ports-and-forts-variant]forts to attack[/url] and [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/608896/initial-ideas-for-squashs-quotmobile-merchantsquot]mobile merchants[/url].  Thankfully, the game is also as visually stunning as it is fun to play.  All the components are top-notch, with the highlight definitely being the gorgeous ship sculpts (although those stinkin' sloops keep capsizing).  Out of frustration with the lack of good pirate games I had begun to design my own, but with the release of this masterpiece, I thankfully do not have to put in all the effort of completing my own design!  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4.5/5  Total: 9/10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Outstanding muti-layered pirate-themed action game. Players assume the roles of ship captains in the Caribbean during the Golden Age of Piracy. Firstly, you have to make a decision whether to opt for a career based around the transportation and trading of goods, or whether to search for ships to attack and steal from. From then on you are committed to finding the best way to profit from your chosen path and by doing this you accumulate money (which can be used in many different ways such as upgrading your ship, repairing it, acquiring rumours etc) and glory points, which are used to determine a victor. Everything in the game works so smoothly from the random availability of goods in each port to the simple and effective means of combat where a certain number of dice are rolled based on your attack strength and the results determine where on your opponents ship receives damage. There is so much going on in this game and there are so many routes to victory (this isn't purely a game where you decide whether to be a pirate or a law abiding merchant and that's it), and you are continually having to adapt to factors affecting your strategy. In short, this is the best game of its kind I've played, a theme-rich action game with a balanced amount of randomness which also rewards strong strategic play.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
