Arrrrrrrrr!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
M&M has a good feel to it, but it's a very long-playing game. To be sure, three of us were beginners, but five hours? The number of parameters in the game are many and somewhat confusing; and, I think, unnecessarily numerous.

While the manual is clear if you internalize the somewhat odd terms, it might have been clearer not to include "Enter port" and "Exit port" under the "Move" action. Taking the turn, exit port, move, enter port has a very incomplete feel to it, as if one lost a turn. The end of the game rather sneaks up on one; it's rather odd that unstashed gold has zero value--after all, this is the gold you're taking out to risk in the world.

The game is a little too driven by the captain one draws. If you don't have a scout of 3, you shouldn't be a pirate however much you want to. I tend to agree that frigate and galleon are unbalanced; my solution would be to drop galleon maneuver to 1 or to give +1 scouting if you have a frigate (you can see farther from the tall masts).

While the game tries to have a realistic feel, it misses that crew displaces cargo. Incorporating this trade-off might force a more definite choice between merchant and marauder. Also, ships were captured (wooden ships were very difficult to sink in combat, barring a magazine explosion).

RATING: 8
Some othe user posted that as rating comment, while our conclusion is vastly different (he rated it a 5  while I rated it a 9). I think his description is really useful.

//Quote
Ok pirate game, but nothing special. Mix of familiar mechanisms like pick-up-and-deliver with random luck from dice rolls and different types of cards. Limited number of important decisions (e.g. going merchant or marauder). The pirate theme is nicely integrated in the game play, but leaves me lukewarm.
//

Don't buy this game for the mechanics. The appeal of this game is the integrated  theme (with solid mechanics) and the experience. I know no other pirate game that allows all that possibilities and still works.  It is (rather) long, it has a high luck factor and the number of decisions is limited (but there are crucial decisions). However the complete package just feels great.

RATING: 8
A sweeping epic of a game that plays very similarly to Sid Meier's Pirates computer gaem. This one is interesting in that, within a loose framework, players have a very open-ended path to follow. They can focus on trading, become pirates, pursue rumors, undertake missions and visit 16 different ports, each with its own special function. And all these things seem to be viable ways to pursue glory points. Starting my rating off at a 7, as I have played this only as a two-player affair, and player interaction is almost non-existent since the map is so large. I suspect this game shines with a busier board and four players - looking forward to finding out. Update: Game rating bumped up a notch after confirming what I suspected ... this game works with two players but shines with four.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
First Impression:
A highly thematic game, that creates an unbelievable narrative after play. However it doesn't flow well, and there are balance issues. 

For starters, the map is too huge even for 4 players, as in a vanilla 10 glory point game, each player will hardly pass through half the map. So player interaction is so poor it almost feels like a solo multiplayer. Even with 4 players I'd be surprised if ship vs ship combat happens more than 1-2 (3max) times during the game. (and that includes player vs npc battles)

Then there are the balance issues.. The game offers two distinct gameplay approaches, a safe one (merchant) and a risky one (pirate). But, for some funny unknown reason the safe one, is also the most rewarding! Add to that the fact that the merchant is both less fun and more time consuming and you get a game of great, yet unfulfilled potential.

OK, so what do the players do with their time>? Buy/Sell goods? Not even that, and that's the biggest game problem. Players WAIT most of their time. It takes about 10 seconds to figure out your next move (strategy starts and ends at set-up, and any tactics elements occur DURING YOUR turn), so you'll have absolutely nothing to do (but watch), while your mates play their turns.

To sum it up, this game suffers from overambitious design, poor balance and boring downtime.
Fortunatelly, not all is lost. Home rules can correct the balance/design issues, but the downtime is trickier. I believe that keeping a captain's log (as in writing what happened during your turn after you end it) is the best all around solution. More plays needed.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Outstanding pirate game. Plays best with three in my experience due to significant downtime with four. I find that lowering the glory points needed to win down to about 6 makes for a nice length game with 4 players. Playing to ten glory points is epic, but quite long. It would seem that playing as a merchant is the easiest way to win, but I need to play a few more times and test a few strategies to know for sure. 

UPDATE- LOOOONG downtime brings this down from a 9 to an 8.5. Great fun- but so much time spent waiting around with 4 players.

Merchants & Marauders lets you live the life of an influential merchant or a dreaded pirate in the Caribbean during the Golden Age of Piracy. Seek your fortune through trade, rumor hunting, missions, and of course, plundering. The game features a unique trade system and a thematic combat system, allowing for critical decisions and intense excitement. Modify your ship, buy impressive vessels, load deadly special ammunitions and hire specialist crew members. Will your captain gain eternal glory and immense wealth - or find his wet grave under the stormy surface of the Caribbean Sea?

RATING: 7
The game has a tentative rating of 7. I have my doubts but thus far, with one play, the game shows promise. Just not sure how much higher the rating can go. On first brush, the game looks sandboxey, but I can also easily see how the game can feel repetitive after a while. There are certainly some routes that are more optimal than others and some sea zones are clearly superior (I am looking at you, Old Providence). In general, if you are a pirate, the extra weapons are a must. Being able to equip yourself to change the die face to a "win" is critical for getting glory points after the plunder. It is not tough, especially if you get 2-3 skulls to achieve the necessary cards. Old Providence is also very well equipped for piracy. That said, the NPC can provide some tension and also blocks the ability of ships to move back and forth.

Overall, the game is undoubtedly thematic and loads of cool stories courtesy of the rumor and mission cards. I love the simplicity of the design and movement, but not the die rolls so much. Combat is not tough to grasp, but there is a lot of die rolling around, even for me.

I certainly would love to play it again to see how the game flows with 2.

RATING: 8
This game has me so torn.  It makes me grin like a kid playing it, really does a good job of emulating Sid Meier's Pirate video game that I loved growing up.  This is a game that tells a story, ports change allegiance, your career could change from lowly merchant to frightening pirate.  The battle system feels convoluted, and I have to relearn it every time I play, it's daunting for new players... but it does offer multiple paths to victory in a battle, and the ability to pull off surprise wins.  

The downsides for me are primarily the downtime.  It can be really dull just watching someone go to a market and choose cards in secret.  It's a long wait if someone is getting into combat.  My other complaints are tied to what make the game great, lots of fiddly things to manage on the board, and rules complexities to relearn each time you play.  People can get lucky and run away with the game and be very hard to prevent... but damn it all if this game isn't fun to play.

The art, miniatures and components are fantastic though.

RATING: 8
It was looking for a publisher, then it found one, then it didn't, then it did again, and finally it has come out.  Slow burn, much?  I've been following this game for a while, which meant I had very high hopes.  I'm not ecstatic about it now that I've gotten the chance to play it, but I'm not disappointed, either. RATING: 8
I had some initial apprehension when author Christian really emphasized that this was not a eurogame, but I went ahead and purchased anyway, because I really wanted to support him after all the crap he went through to get this published. He deserves a hit.

And I think it delivers. It's just plain fun to sail around, pick up rumours, events, trade goods, or go plain ol' buccaneering on someone's %^&. :D We mostly just attack the NPC's rather than each other, but it still works that way.

It's a testament to the great design that this is already one of the most houseruled games on BGG. This isn't a fault, it's a strength. You can lengthen the game, shorten it, add players, make combat easier, harder, more or less frequent, tweak the balance between playing as a merchant vs a pirate based on how you or your group plays. Just amazing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I have waited a long time for the perfect Pirate game to come along and Merchants & Marauders does not disappoint.  On the surface it seems pretty light - move your ships, buy and sell goods and try to stay out of trouble.  It is certainly possible (and maybe a little bit easier) to eke out a win this way.  But it is so much fun taking the pirate route.  You get to chase your foes around the Caribbean blasting them with grape shot and plundering their vessels.  You still need to be careful though - the NPC naval ships are not to be taken lightly, and with bounties on your head you just never know when one of your opponents might try to take you on for the reward.  What can I say?  Fun, fun, fun!!!  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I have owned this game for a few years now and it has become my favorite board game of all time. I have played several times with different groups of people and look forward to playing this as much as possible for years and years. The solo variant rules created by Woelf (which are posted in the Merchants and Marauders forum) are fantastic. I enjoy playing this game solo more than I enjoy playing other games that were designed as solitaire games. This is more of a thematic adventure game than a strategy game, but using good strategy is certainly key to winning the game.

I feel compelled to address a couple of the issues people have brought up in negative reviews. First, I have read multiple times that people feel there are no meaningful decisions.  One reviewer even went so far as to say that all you do is buy cargo, move, then sell. I have to ask myself "What game are these people playing?!" Nothing could be further from the truth. In fact, the variety of choices laid out before a player on any given turn is, in my opinion, one of the things that makes this game really special.  

If I had just bought two cargo of, say, spices on my previous turn, I would have a slew of choices before me on my current turn: should I immediately try to unload these in a port where spices are not in demand (for a small profit) in order to get a different kind of cargo? should I go to another port and try to get more spices and then continue on to sell them later? should I take what I have to a port where spices are in demand and sell there even though I only have 2 spices? since there is a pirate sailing around near that sea zone I want to get to, should I turtle up and cower here waiting for it to move, or should I take the risk and hope he won't find me or that I'll be able to escape if he does find me...or should I change plans altogether so I don't have to deal with that pirate? should I forget about these spices and try to take advantage of that vulnerable merchant ship over there? should I attack my buddy's ship that just got a little too close to me? should I try to find a nice juicy rumor that could net me a nice earning of gold, an abandoned ship, or cool abilities that will help me throughout the game? should I go claim that mission that the governor of San Juan is sponsoring wherein I scout out my pirate buddy and lead the Spanish navy to him? should I focus on upgrading my ship so that it can become the strongest ship sailing the seas and I can go hunting? should I sail to Port Royal to attempt to recruit that Master Carpenter to join my crew? should I try to hunt down that pirate over there to earn a nice gold reward?

To me the possibilities are HUGE and if people are somehow missing all of that, I can only conclude that they either don't understand this game or they are pre-disposed not to like games that are different from what they are familiar with.  

The other thing I have read quite a few times is that being a merchant (rather than a pirate) is an auto win.  First of all, there is nothing that says a player must be either a merchant OR a pirate, i.e. you don't have to just be one or the other. There are numerous ways for players to engage in piracy and also to have their criminal deeds forgiven. When I last played with serious gamer friends, the guy who won did an awesome job of balancing trading/merchanting with preying on the weak when the right opportunities came along. Pirates have the ability to raid merchants which are plentiful when the game begins and, in my opinion, allows the players who choose piracy right off the bat to get a nice head start (sometimes merchants will have to traverse the entire Caribbean to get to a port where there cargo of sugar is in demand). Some missions, like acquiring a Letter of Marque, are only available to players that have engaged in piracy so players that choose to be strictly merchants will miss those opportunities. The max number of game-controlled pirates is 2, while the max number of game-controlled naval ships is 4, meaning that while there are always more ships trying to hunt down pirates than there are pirates hunting down merchants, there is also more opportunity for pirate players to attack and plunder ships. In my opinion, the balance between all of possible choices and paths that players can take to victory is shockingly balanced. It is not perfect, but a player can certainly win any way he or she wants to if they plan well, take the right risks, and get lucky to have some things go their way.  Being a merchant is in no way an auto win.  

Feel free to PM me if you have questions and are on the fence about buying this game.  I'll try to provide an honest assessment of if you'd enjoy it or not. It's definitely not for everyone, but for the right crowd this game is simply phenomenal.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Merchants & Marauders recreates almost every single aspect of the PC classic "Sid Meier's Pirates!", but in boardgame form. The only things missing are the town raids, yet I have a feeling even those will be coming down the line at some point, in an expansion box. The game can be a little challenging to teach, mostly due to all of the different ship upgrades and a somewhat unintuitive combat system. Once you get the hang of it however, it plays quite smoothly. 

As with most games that feature player vs. player combat, there can be some downtime issues. Generally speaking though, there is usually plenty of planning to fill the time. The game offers an incredible amount of freedom, allowing you to chase after Glory points however you choose. The rules also never lock you into a strategy. You can play the whole game as a crafty merchant and then jump into piracy at the drop of a hat to take advantage of an easy target. This flexibility gives the game its incredible flavor and ultimately will make it an Ameritrash classic.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
My opinion isn't favorable.  The merchant strategy, in particular, is mindless and repetitive: sell in-demand goods three at a time for glory points, buy goods cheaply (if possible) that are in demand in nearby ports, and stay out of attacking range of marauding pirates.

There was a lot of downtime in our first session (4 players, 4+ hours), which certainly didn't do much to improve my impression of the game.  Once players were comfortable with the way that ports worked, we finally sped things along by having players take their turns while other players were busy with their port actions. Having too many players take their turns simultaneously can get confusing, though - which happened a number of times.

In terms of mechanics, I was surprised to find a number of similarities (e.g., port usage, the earning of enemy status with different countries, country warfare) between Merchants & Marauders and [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/13347/plunder]Plunder[/url], the small-box pirate game released in 2004. But by no means are the games identical.  The board in Plunder is "built" during the game (with cards) using an exploring mechanic, whereas in M&M the board is fixed.  And at its core, Plunder is about card management; M&M, in contrast, is a dice game.  Finally, combat in Plunder is much more lethal: If neither player escapes, one of the captains is definitely taking a coral nap in the deep blue.  In M&M, the losing player has a good chance of limping away so that s/he can put into port for repairs and live to loot another day.

As far as the evolution of all-things-pirate, M&M definitely improves upon some of Plunder's shortcomings (e.g., the in-demand good at a specific port changes after each sale at that port), but the overall level of fun is approximately the same.  Consequently, given the tremendous difference in playtime between the two games (4 hours vs. 90 minutes), I have to say that I prefer Plunder.  Truthfully, though, neither game is particularly engrossing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is all-around just plain awesome, and it sits comfortably at the top of my list of favorite games.


There are a lot of rules to keep track of and the sheer number of options can seem overwhelming at first, but it's all intertwined so perfectly with the theme that everything flows very smoothly once you get into it.  Plus the included reference sheet covers everything you could possibly need, so you really don't need to memorize much at all.

Visually, this is a beautifully produced game.   The artwork is fantastic, and the miniatures are superb whether you decide to paint them or not.  The tokens are all nice thick cardboard, and the cards, while small, have the nice linen finish so they should last a long time.   If you feel the desperate need to sleeve something the cargo cards could benefit, but most of the others barely ever get shuffled or passed around so sleeves are unnecessary for them.


The negatives are few and are fairly minor, but to some people they can be deal-breakers:
--Downtime between turns can sometimes be a factor, but it's usually a symptom of slow decision making.   If you pay attention during other players' turns and plan ahead a bit, most of that issue goes away.   And for everyone's sake, turn off your damn phone/iPad/etc. and put it away.
--Luck can be a factor in the game, with plenty of dice rolls and card draws, but there are countless ways to mitigate or at least minimize that luck so it's not going to get in your way unless you're one of those players that absolutely despise all randomness/luck in any form.
--Game time is approximately 45 minutes per player, although with experienced players that time will drop significantly.    I've completed entire 2-player games in about an hour more than once [i](not counting setup or takedown, which adds maybe 5-10 minutes on each end)[/i].



I highly recommend this game for anyone, not just fans of Pirate games.  

If you already like Pirate games, you will not find a better one than this.

RATING: 8.75
Whilst I am not a fan of the dice rolling mechanic, Merchants & Merauders have utilised this mechanic rather well. It is certainly suited to the uncertain career of a pirate. Various risk mitigating mechanics have also been built into the game for those who dislike pure dice rolling.

The rules are on the fiddly side, but once players know them well, the game should flow smoothly and game time kept low. There are numerous ways to earn the required 10 glory points for victory, and that provides some variety in the game.

Interaction may be lower for 2 player games, but the presence of non-player captains maintain the tension to a large extent.

Last but not least, the artwork and quality of game components are excellent.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.75
The pirate game you've been waiting for, if you've been waiting for a game that makes you feel like a pirate... without also feeling like a bookkeeper.  Or when you simply want to outwit the enemy, and continue peacefully and prosperously on your merchant's way.

Fast-paced, and multi-pronged.  Each avenue to victory is viable, and every engagement has the potential to go horribly wrong or fantastically right!

Plus, while the basic rules are easy enough (with a little help from your forum friends) to grasp the game has an excellent amount of grit and complexity.  This makes the replay value much higher than it might be if the game were A) shorter, or B) less complex.

It's not all 'bang-bang, I win; bang-bang, you lose'.  Rather there are subtleties of strategy to be thought out and executed (or foiled), and even a major setback (you've lost your ship, your cargo and your captain...feel free to start again) doesn't always, or even usually, spell defeat.  The game system itself presents major obstacles for either side.  Let alone your fellow players...who invariably throw a wrench in your works.

Great game!  And beautifully presented.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

It has pirates. 'Nuff said.

If there is a complaint it would be that it's a WEE bit fiddly in terms of rule complexity, but even that isn't a turn-off for me particularly when you consider that there isn't anything that needs to be done "better."  

There are a few variants (both officially approved) that are worth playing, but even if you ignore them the game is flat out wonderful.

RATING: 7.5
Can be a simple 'pick up and deliver' game, and it does that well enough - buy low, sell high, accrue lots of cash. But take the leap into piracy and the game really shines. Other players become fearful of ending their turn at sea in case you rob them blind, and it's WAY more satisfying.
